<li>Low temperature tempering (<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>150</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">150^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">15</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>250</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">250^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">25</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>).</li>
<li>Medium temperature tempering (<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>350</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">350^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">35</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>450</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">450^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">45</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>).</li>
<li>High temperature tempering (<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>500</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">500^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">50</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>650</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">650^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">65</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>).</li>
</ol>
<p>In Figure 1.15, the shaded areas a, b, and c represent the tempering regions in iron-carbon diagram. A tempering process relives residual stresses, improves ductility, gives toughness by the reduction of hardness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="case-hardening">Case hardening<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#case-hardening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Case hardening is a heat treatment process in which the low carbon steel (0.1%C) is heated to red hot and the content of carbon or nitrogen or both on the outer shell of the workpiece is increased by forcing to absorb from the surrounding to the surface for certain depth by diffusion. The outer shell is hardened as done in the hardening process. Thus, by getting the hardened surface and a ductile core, a machine part gets high wear resistance as well as heavy dynamic load bearing</p>
<p>capacity. The commonly used case hardening processes are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Carburizing</li>
<li>Nitriding</li>
<li>Cyaniding</li>
<li>Carbo-nitriding</li>
</ol>
<p>In carburizing process the percentage of carbon in the outer shell is increased to about 1%. The nitriding process adds nitrogen to the outer shell of certain steels containing aluminium and chromium. In cyaniding process both carbon and nitrogen are added to the surface by using a liquid bath, whereas in carbo-nitriding, the same is added by gas atmosphere.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surface-hardening">Surface hardening<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surface-hardening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In surface hardening, only the selected surface is subjected to heating, whereas in case hardening the whole object is brought to the hardening temperature. The hardening property to the surface is obtained to the steel by adding carbon and nitrogen. The heating of surface is done by the following methods.</p>
<ol>
<li>Induction hardening</li>
<li>Flame hardening.</li>
<li>Laser beam hardening</li>
<li>Electron beam hardening.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-6-2-heat-treatment-of-nonferrous-metals">1.6.2 Heat Treatment of Nonferrous Metals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-6-2-heat-treatment-of-nonferrous-metals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The heat treatment of nonferrous metals is done for strengthening the metal. Single-phase metals can be strengthened by solid solution hardening process, while strain hardening is used to strengthen ductile metals. The most widely used and effective method for nonferrous metals and alloys is precipitation hardening or age hardening. To understand the various heat treatment processes clearly and to practice them, one must have deep knowledge in metallurgy and the related processes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-6-3-cold-working-of-metals">1.6.3 Cold Working of Metals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-6-3-cold-working-of-metals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Shaping of metal by plastic deformation can be done in cold state or hot state. If the mechanical working of metals is done below the recrystallization temperature, it is named as cold working. For steel, the mechanical working below the lower critical temperature (A1 line in Figure 1.15) of about 700°C is considered as working in cold state. Remember, only a few metals and alloys can be reasonably cold worked.</p>
<p>To understand the behaviour of metal in cold working, one must know about the structure of metal. A metal is made up of irregular grains of different size. In cold working of metals, the grain structure changes resulting the grain fragmentation and distortion. The change of shape of metal can occur only if the stress exceeds the elastic limit. In cold state, metal has higher elastic limit, hence much force has to be applied to affect deformation. There is no recrystallization of distorted grains during a cold working, but results increase of tensile strength, hardness and reduction of ductility of metal. This phenomenon of cold working is known as work hardening or strain hardening. In order to bring the metal back to its initial state, heat treatment is to be applied. Annealing is the heat treatment used to reduce the work hardening of metal. Cold working has the following advantages.</p>
<ol>
<li>There is no need of heating of metal, so working expense is reduced.</li>
<li>Since the workpiece is at room temperature, the work handling, inspection and other related activities are simple and easy.</li>
<li>Very good surface finish with no scale is obtained.</li>
<li>The hardness and tensile strength of the metal are increased.</li>
<li>Better accuracy in dimension can be maintained.</li>
</ol>
<p>Compared to the advantages, the drawback of cold working is the work hardening. Distortion of grains removes ductility and fracture starts after certain level of deformation. Annealing is the only process to remove this hardness. Cold working is very well used as a finishing process to get better surface finish, dimensional accuracy and hardness. Cold rolling, cold extrusion, press working, wire drawing, tube drawing, cold heading, etc., are some of the popular cold working processes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-6-4-hot-working-of-metals">1.6.4 Hot Working of Metals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-6-4-hot-working-of-metals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hot working is conducted at a temperature above the recrystallization point of the metal. For steels, this temperature is about 100°C above the higher critical point (A3) i.e. slightly above 800°C. Since the temperature is above the recrystallization point, the resistance to deformation is lowered considerably and grain recovery occurs continuously as the</p>
<p>grains are elongated. High section reduction against less force application is possible in short time. The advantages of hot working are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Less force is to be applied and large deformation of section is obtained.</li>
<li>Porosity of metal is largely eliminated by welding of metal in the hot plastic state.</li>
<li>Directional properties resulting fibre structure is obtained (Example is drop forging).</li>
<li>The full range of deformation is completed in the shortest time.</li>
<li>Hot working is economical for shapes requiring more reduction, even though there is the expense for heating.</li>
</ol>
<p>Compared to the above advantages, hot working has some limitations. They are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Heating is an expensive process and care should be taken to avoid burning of metal.</li>
<li>Scale formation is severe and reduces the metal surface finish, hence hot working is difficult for objects having more surface area like plates and sheets.</li>
<li>Due to the shrinkage during cooling and the scale formation, the dimensional accuracy of a hot worked product is less.</li>
<li>In hot working, the handling of metal is difficult and maintenance expense of machines are high due to working at high temperatures.</li>
</ol>
<p>The advantages of hot working are always prominent than the limitations, for large and heavy products. So, hot working is very well used for shaping metal, especially steel from the initial metal ingot to the customer sections like angle, channel, beam, rod, etc. The hot working method is used in rolling, forging, extrusion, deep drawing, spinning, etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-6-5-shot-peening">1.6.5 Shot Peening<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-6-5-shot-peening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Shot peening is one among the processes which change the material properties, effectively on the surface. The process basically consists of directing a blast of metal shots to the surface of a workpiece. The throwing of shots at high velocity is done by either the use of a pressurized air jet or high speed rotation of a wheel as in pumping. The peening action of shots gives compression of the surface of the workpiece. This develops hardness to the surface, improves the strength and adds fatigue resistance of the workpiece.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-7-materials-for-workshop-practice">1.7 Materials for Workshop Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-7-materials-for-workshop-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A material can be defined as that out of which anything is or may be made. A large number of materials are used in engineering. These can be broadly grouped as metals and nonmetals. To select the appropriate material for a job, the engineer must know about the properties, cost, availability, etc., of engineering materials. The following sections give a brief introduction to the materials used for workshop processes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-7-1-classification-of-engineering-materials">1.7.1 Classification of Engineering Materials<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-7-1-classification-of-engineering-materials" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The materials used for engineering can be broadly classified into the following categories:</p>
<ol>
<li>Metals</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Ferrous metals</p>
<p>(i) Wrought iron
(ii) Cast iron
(iii) Plain carbon steels
(iv) Low alloy steels
(v) High alloy steels</p>
<p>(b) Nonferrous metals and alloys</p>
<p>(i) Copper
(ii) Aluminium
(iii) Lead
(iv) Magnesium
(v) Nickel
(vi) Tin
(vii) Zinc
(viii) Cadmium, antimony, etc.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Organic materials</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Plastics</p>
<p>(i) Thermo plastics
(ii) Thermosetting plastics</p>
<p>(b) Rubber</p>
<p>(i) Natural rubber</p>
<p>(i) Synthetic rubber</p>
<p>(c) Wood</p>
<p>(d) Miscellaneous organic materials like fuels, lubricants, paints, textiles, adhesives, explosives etc.
3. Ceramic materials</p>
<p>(a) Sand</p>
<p>(b) Glass</p>
<p>(c) Refractories</p>
<p>(d) Insulators</p>
<p>(e) Miscellaneous ceramic items, like abrasive, bricks, cement, asbestos, etc.</p>
<p>Ferrous and nonferrous metals</p>
<p>The metals that are commonly used in workshops can be broadly classified as ferrous metals and nonferrous metals.</p>
<p>Ferrous metals</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Grey cast iron</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Low carbon (mild) steel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Medium carbon steel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High carbon steel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alloy steel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stainless steel</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Nonferrous metals</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>
<p>Copper</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Brass</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bronze</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aluminium and its alloys</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Grey cast iron: Grey cast iron is the commonly used material for machine body, base plates, pump casing, electric motor casing, etc. In grey cast iron, the carbon of about 2 to 4% is found in the form of graphite. The graphite form gives grey appearance and hence the metal is called grey cast iron. Cast iron is the outproduct of the furnace called cupola. There are other furnaces like pit furnace, induction furnace or arc furnace which are used to melt cast iron. The machine parts produced using this metal is initially cast by foundry process and then machined to the required dimension and finish. In cast iron there are constituents like silicon (1 to 3%), sulphur (0..02 to 0.15%), phosphorus (1%), etc., other than the carbon. Depending on them, the cast iron is graded and selected for various duties. Cast iron is brittle and has low capacity to take tensile loads, but very good for handling compressive stresses. Grey cast iron has good machinability and no ductility. The melting point is low compared to steel, at the same time intricate shapes can be cast without difficulty at low expense. Because of all these properties grey cast iron is very well used for heavy machine bodies and parts, which are subjected to high compressive loads.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Low carbon (mild) steel: Low carbon steel which is also called as mild steel (MS) is an alloy of iron and carbon. The carbon content varies from 0.05 to 0.15 percentage for dead mild steel and 0.15 to 0.3 percentage for mild steel. The dead mild steel is very much ductile and is used for making various components like sheets, strips, wires, rods etc. The mild steel (0.15 to 0.3%C) is used for making various structural sections like angles, channels, beams, rods, boiler plates, pins, axles, etc. This family of steel is the most common metal used by engineers for manufacturing, such as steel structures, steel furniture, steel for reinforced concrete, various welded fabrications, forgings, machine parts, etc. The relative use comes to about 50% of the total worldwide use of metal.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Medium carbon steel: For medium carbon steel, the carbon percentage varies from 0.3 to 0.8 percent. These steels have better strength and not very easy to shape as mild steel. The hardness is slightly higher and the ductility is poor. The machine parts requiring strength like springs automobile parts, shafts, dies for forging, etc., are made from medium carbon steels. About 20% of the worldwide use of metal is covered by this family of steel.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High carbon steel: In high carbon steel, the carbon percentage varies from 0.8 to 1.5. A high percentage of carbon gives hardness and strength to the metal. They can be heat-treated to get the required properties. High carbon steels are used mainly for tools like chisels, hammers, dies, punches, broaches, reamers, drills, taps, etc., and machine parts like springs, mandrels and similar parts requiring high strength and hardness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alloy steels: In addition to carbon, other elements like nickel, chromium vanadium, tungsten, etc., are added in small percentages to attain certain special properties to the steel. Such steels are called alloy steels. According to the Indian standards, alloy steels are classified into the following categories:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>(i) Low alloy steels which are having alloying elements up to 5%.</p>
<p>(ii) Medium alloy steels, which are having 5 to 10% alloying elements.</p>
<p>(iii) High alloy steels, which are having alloying elements more than 10%.</p>
<p>Nickel, chromium and manganese are the principal alloy elements in these steels. Tungsten, molybdenum, titanium, vanadium, etc., are added in small proportions. Alloy steels are used for various structures and machine parts subjected to heavy static and dynamic loads.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>
<p>Stainless steel: Corrosion resistant steels are generally known as stainless steels. The alloying element (chromium) is added for about 4 to 6% to low carbon steels for producing fairly good corrosion resistant steels. For high resistance to corrosion and fine appearance the chromium percentage has to be increased to a range of 11 to 27%. Sometimes other elements like nickel, manganese, silicon are also added in small percentages to get various desired properties. Stainless steels with chromium content above 12% is used for utensils, diary equipment, food processing units, chemical industries, surgical equipment, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Copper: Copper containing impurities up to 0.1% is used for electrical purposes. This copper has high electrical as well as thermal conductivity and good corrosion resistance. The metal is easy to shape and has moderate strength. The inherent properties of copper direct to wide applications, such as electrical conductors, steam pipes, containers, house hold utensils, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Brass: The alloy of copper and zinc is called brass. The alloy containing up to 37% zinc is called alpha brass and it is very ductile and can be easily cold-worked. Alpha brass can be used for producing sheets, wires, deep drawn tubes and shapes. As the zinc percentage increases (from 33 to 47%) the strength increases, but the ductility reduces. Such a brass is called alpha beta brass and is used for hot-working. Brasses have high resistance to corrosion, reasonable electrical conductivity and satisfactory thermal conductivity. It is easily machinable and can work as good bearing material giving less friction. Because of these inherent properties, brasses of various proportions are very well used for electrical connectors, bearings, corrosion resistant material for various chemical equipment, household utensils, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bronze: Bronze is considered basically as an alloy of copper and tin. It has superior mechanical properties and corrosion resistance than brass. Bronze is comparatively hard and resists surface wear. It can be shaped by mechanical working or machining similar to brass. Bronze of various compositions containing other alloying elements of small percentages are widely used for engineering purposes. Phosphor bronze, gun metal, bell metal, silver bronze, aluminium bronze, etc. are some of the common types of bronzes in use. For example, a type of phosphor bronze containing 11% tin and 0.3% phosphor, is used for bearings, gears, nuts, machine screws, etc. Gun metal is the best quality of bronze and contains 88% copper, 10% tin 2% zinc and small percentages of other alloys like phosphorus, lead, etc. It is highly resistant to corrosion and is used for small size valves, bearings, pipe line fittings, glands, marine castings, etc. This particular types of brass was used earlier as the gun barrel material and hence, it was called as gun metal. The bronze group of alloys has several advantages but is an expensive material than cast iron, steel and even brass.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aluminium and its alloys: Aluminium is a light metal having density of about 2.7. It is highly malleable and ductile and is a good conductor of heat and electricity. Shaping of aluminium products by mechanical working and machining are easy. To improve the properties and strength, aluminium is alloyed with various elements like copper, chromium, nickel, iron, zinc, manganese, silver, etc. Duralumin is a type of aluminium alloy used for automobile parts, aircraft parts, light weight structures, extruded sections, sheets, bars, tubes, rivets, etc. It contains approximately 4% Cu, 0.5% Mg, 0.5% Mn, 0.5% Fe or Si and the balance aluminium. A general purpose aluminium casting alloy has a proportion of 13.5% Zn, 3% Cu and the balance Al. Being a light metal of low cost, the use of aluminium for aircrafts, automobiles, portable equipment, moving machine parts like piston, etc. is increasing day by day in the modern world.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cutting-tool-materials">Cutting tool materials<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cutting-tool-materials" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The tool materials used in workshops are of different types depending on the requirements. In general, a cutting tool material may have the following properties.</p>
<ol>
<li>It should have high hardness more than that of the material being cut.</li>
<li>It should have toughness to resist fracture and cutting stresses.</li>
<li>It should have ability to keep the strength at high temperatures at the cutting point.</li>
<li>It should have ability to absorb shocks without permanent deformation.</li>
<li>It should have strength to resist disintegration of fine cutting edges.</li>
</ol>
<p>The types of cutting tool materials are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>High carbon steels</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High speed steels</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cast nonferrous alloys</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Carbides</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ceramic tools</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diamond</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High carbon steels: This is the oldest form of cutting tool material having carbon 0.8 to 1.2%. They have poor metal cutting ability at high speed. They are suitable to cut wood and soft metals only.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High speed steel (H.S.S.): This is a high alloy steel which can be used to cut metal at a cutting speed of 2 to 3 times that of high carbon steel. The most commonly used H.S.S. has a composition called 18-4-1 (tungsten 18%, chromium 4% vanadium 1%, carbon 0.7% and balance iron.) The H.S.S. is used for cutting tools in lathes, shapers, planers, milling machines, drilling machines, broaching machines, etc. There is another composition called super or cobalt high speed steel (cobalt 12%, tungsten 20%, chromium 4% vanadium 2%, carbon 0.8% and the balance iron). This super H.S.S. has better hardness and can be safely cut at high temperatures like 620°C.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cast nonferrous alloys: Nonferrous alloys are used as cutting tool material, after casting the tool shape and sharpening by grinding. Some of the popular trade names of these tool materials are mentioned below:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stellite</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gormet</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Crobalt</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tantung</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The ingredients of the tool material having trade name stellite are chromium 25 to 35%, Tungsten 4 to 25%, carbon 1 to 3% and the balance is cobalt 40 to 50%. The cast nonferrous alloys are strong tool material and can be used for cutting speeds two times higher than that of H.S.S. The cutting temperature at tool tip can go up to 900°C. The mechanical properties are largely determined by the degree of chilling given in casting.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Carbides: Carbide tools are nonferrous alloys having tungsten as the main ingredient. A typical composition of carbide tool is tungsten carbide 82%, titanium carbide 10%, and cobalt 8%. This tool is very good for machining steel. The tool tips are shaped as bits of shapes like triangle, square, round, etc., by sintering process as in powder metallurgy. Then the bits are brazed or mechanically fixed on the tool shank.</li>
</ol>
<p>Carbide tool tips are extremely hard and can retain hardness up to 1200°C. They have less friction against cutting and the cutting speeds can be of high values of 2 to 2.5 times that of H.S.S. Carbide tools are excellent for heavy cuts in steel and cast iron. Their higher wear resistance makes them suitable for use as dies and punches in press working.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Ceramic tools: Ceramic tools are made as bits using various boron-nitride powders. The tool bits are shaped by sintering process at 1700°C. Ceramic tools can be operated at cutting speeds 2 to 3 times that of tungsten carbide tools. They are very hard and extremely brittle. Ceramic tools are used as throwaway bits for high speed finish turning operations. For getting long tool life for ceramic tools, the machine should not produce shock loads and vibrations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diamond: Diamond is the hardest material and is used as single point cutting tool for light and finish machining at high speeds. Materials that are difficult to cut due to high hardness are machined using diamond tools. Diamond tools can give very high finish and dimensional accuracy in machining.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="exercises">EXERCISES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exercises" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="questions-for-viva-voce">Questions for Viva Voce<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions-for-viva-voce" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="answer-the-following-questions">Answer the following questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#answer-the-following-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="a-primary-shaping-processes">(A) Primary shaping processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-primary-shaping-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>

<li>What are the advantages of machine parts produced by</li>
</ol>

7. Give the names of 3 machine parts produced only by forging. Why they are shaped by forging?

9. What is meant by wire drawing? Give the areas of application of the process.

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-secondary-shaping-processes">(B) Secondary shaping processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-secondary-shaping-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-joining-processes">(C) Joining processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-joining-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-surface-finishing-processes">(D) Surface finishing processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-surface-finishing-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="e-processes-changing-the-material-properties">(E) Processes changing the material properties<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-processes-changing-the-material-properties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="f-materials-for-workshop-practice">(F) Materials for workshop practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f-materials-for-workshop-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Classify the materials used for engineering practice.</li>
<li>Give a list of metals generally used in workshops.</li>
<li>What is meant by cast iron? Explain the useful properties of this metal.</li>
<li>What is meant by mild steel? Give the areas of application and the importance of this metal.</li>
</ol>
<p>Distinguish between high carbon steels and alloys steels.
6. What is meant by stainless steel?
7. Explain briefly about copper and its alloys.
8. Describe the importance of aluminium and its alloys in engineering.
9. Give a list of cutting tool materials used in workshops.
10. What is meant by H.S.S.? Give the uses of the metal.

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>2</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="workshop-practice-and-record-writing">Workshop Practice and Record Writing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#workshop-practice-and-record-writing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An engineering student has to study various theory topics in manufacturing technology and machining processes during his course. Many of the workshop techniques involved in these areas can only be familiarized by practical experience, study on the spot, and by contacts with experienced craftsmen. The theory part that a student has studied, can be physically experienced in a good workshop practice to a reasonable extent. The behaviour of materials, use of tools, methods of operations, control procedures, etc., can be realized by this practice. These experiences add confidence to solve many engineering problems and to make decisions in his future career.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-1-workshop-processes-for-practice">2.1 Workshop Processes for Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-1-workshop-processes-for-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The areas in which the engineering students are given workshop practice, can be broadly divided into two sections as mentioned below.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Hand-working processes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Machining processes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Hand working processes</strong>: The shaping of a part of an equipment or machine by hand operations using hand tools or equipment, can be considered as hand-working process. The commonly practiced hand-working processes are mentioned below:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fitting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Welding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Steel metal works</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Carpentry</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Smithy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foundry</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Machining processes</strong>: Using metal-cutting machine tools, the machining operations are executed to shape parts. The loading of the workpiece, control of the machining operations, the unloading and inspection are done manually. The conventional machining operations practised are as follows:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Turning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drilling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shaping</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Slotting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Milling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Grinding</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The theory and practice of various hand-working processes as well as machining processes are explained in the Modules B and C respectively.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-2-safety-measures">2.2 Safety Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-safety-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Safety is the primary requirement that a worker or student should learn before he starts working in a workshop. A worker or student can easily learn how to work safely. Rules and regulations, mechanical guards and devices, posters and lectures about safety measures are very important, but they will never replace intelligent precautions taken by the worker or student in doing his work. A good and safe worker is the one, who is safety-conscious and always adopts safe and accepted procedures. The following are the types of safety measures to be considered in a workshop.</p>
<ol>
<li>Safety of the worker</li>
<li>Safety of the job</li>
<li>Safety of machines, tools and equipment</li>
</ol>
<p>To maintain safe working conditions and to avoid accidents, different</p>
<p>types of safety measures are taken, depending upon the type and seriousness of accident that may happen. A student, who is going to practice in workshops, has to know the following important safety measures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wear-safe-clothing">Wear safe clothing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wear-safe-clothing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wear tight shirt or dress while working inside the workshop. For good protection of the clothing, shop apron may be worn. Wear shoes with thick soles. Do not wear rings, watches, bracelets, or other jewellery that could get caught in moving machine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintain-good-housekeeping-habit">Maintain good housekeeping habit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintain-good-housekeeping-habit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Keep the workshop floor free of oil, grease or any other liquid. Store materials in such a way that they cannot cause hazards. Do not leave tools or workpieces on the work bench or table of machine. They should be kept in the places allotted for them. Clean the work bench or machine after a work and place the scrap in the scrap box.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="follow-the-general-safety-measures">Follow the general safety measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#follow-the-general-safety-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>While working with machines, the guards should be in position. Replace them immediately after repairs, if any. Do not try to clean or repair a machine, if it is in motion. Cutting tools and workpiece on any machine should be clamped securely before starting. An operator of a machine should not lean against a machine. He should avoid unnecessary talking, while operating the machine. Sufficient light should be provided at the working area.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="take-precaution-while-using-hand-tools">Take precaution while using hand tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#take-precaution-while-using-hand-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Hammers: Do not use a hammer, unless the head is tightly fixed to the handle. Place the hammer on the bench carefully in the proper position. A falling hammer can cause serious foot injuries. Never strike two hammers together, because the faces of hammers are very hard and blow may cause a chip to break off, while hammering.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chisels: While hammering on a chisel, care should be taken to get the blow correctly on the striking head (back) of the chisel, otherwise, it may cause injury to the chisel holding hand. Mushroomed striking head of the chisel should be removed by grinding. The cut edges are often sharp and may cause injury to hand. They may be removed by filing or grinding.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Files: Never use files without proper handles. The surface of the file should be clean and dirt-free. Never hammer on a file or use the file for hammering, because files are made of very brittle material.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Saw: Do not test the sharpness of the blade of a saw by running a finger across the teeth. While using a saw, check whether there is proper tension of the blade. Do not apply heavy pressure or sideways force on the saw, because it may break the blade and even cause injury to hand.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="take-precaution-while-operating-machine-tools">Take precaution while operating machine tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#take-precaution-while-operating-machine-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Drilling machine: Fix the drill bit tightly on the chuck and remove the tightening key. Clamp the workpiece on the machine vice before starting drilling. The drilling surface should be perpendicular to the axis of rotation of the bit. A punch mark at the position of drilling can give accuracy in hole location. While drilling of small diameters, (less than 5 mm) the axial load should be low in order to protect the bit from breaking. Clean the chips from the machine table using a brush.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lathe: Before starting the machine, clamp the work on the chuck solidly. Turn the chuck or face plate by hand to inspect the working, prior to the starting of machine. Keep the machine clear of tools and then start. Do not stop the rotation of chuck by hand. Take measurements only after stopping the machine. Do not remove chips by hand; use brush or pliers if necessary, to remove long chips. While working on the lathe, only the operator has to switch on/off the machine, and not by a second person.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Grinding machine: Wear goggles or a face shield while grinding on a grinding machine. The wheel-guard and tool-rest should be fitted on the machine properly. While grinding, do not press the work or tool too much on the wheel and it should be held firmly by hand. Never operate a grinding wheel at speeds higher than that recommended by the manufacturer.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-3-preparing-for-the-workshop-practice">2.3 Preparing for the Workshop Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-3-preparing-for-the-workshop-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An engineering student who is going to do workshop practice, has to prepare the following prior to practice:</p>
<ol>
<li>The student has to possess the following materials:</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Work record of A4 size.</p>
<p>(b) Fair record approved by the workshop authorities.</p>
<p>(c) Pen, clutch pencil, eraser and a straight edge.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Students are advised to wear tight dress, preferably pants and shirts. Girl, students have to tie their hair and tuck neatly as a precaution against being caught against moving machine parts. For good protection of clothing, a shop apron of dark colour</li>
</ol>
<p>may also be worn. Wearing of shoes instead of slippers is also recommended for the safety of legs from sharp and hot chips and material other waste.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Study the relevant theory about the process, tools, equipment and the material being used for the practice. Usually the students are given a study of the workshop tools and equipment prior to the practice.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-4-writing-of-the-work-record">2.4 Writing of the Work Record<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-writing-of-the-work-record" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A work record is the write-up and sketches prepared by the student along with the study of tools and equipment or workshop practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-4-1-writing-of-work-record-for-a-study">2.4.1 Writing of Work Record for a Study<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-1-writing-of-work-record-for-a-study" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Before starting the actual practice in a workshop, the instructor gives description about the different types of tools and equipment used for cutting, holding, measuring, etc. Students are allowed to handle the tools and thus to become familiar with the shape, name of parts, and the method of using them. After the study, the students are required to prepare the work record of the study. The suggested layout of the work record is shown in Figure 2.1.</p>
<ol>
<li>Heading: It should be written by using capital letters on the top portion of the 1st right side (facing) page.</li>
<li>Serial number and date: It should be written in the top portion of the left side margin of the 1st right side page.</li>
<li>Aim: Objective of the study is to be written on the right side page as the first paragraph.</li>
<li>Tools and equipment: The list of tools and equipment studied showing the detailed specification, has to be furnished as the second paragraph under the title.</li>
<li>Neat sketches of the tools and equipment have to be prepared using pencil on the left hand pages. The name of parts should be marked on them. The appropriate caption should be written below each drawing.</li>
<li>A brief description of each tool or equipment studied has to be prepared on the right side pages, under an underlined subheading.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-4495e042.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg">
FIGURE 2.1 Layout of work record/fair record for a study.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-8092061e.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<p>Each student has to prepare the work record on the lines indicated above after conducting the study and get it approved by the instructor, after correction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-4-2-writing-of-work-record-for-a-practice">2.4.2 Writing of Work Record for a Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-2-writing-of-work-record-for-a-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Similar to study, a work record has to be prepared for workshop practice also. In this work record, a student copies the drawing of the model to be completed and prepares a sketch of the raw material piece to be used for the model. The list of tools to be used and other raw materials, special requirements, etc., if any, are also noted. The procedure is written after completing the model. The suggested layout of the work record for a practice is shown in Figure 2.2.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Heading, serial number with date, and aim are similar to that given in the study.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Work material: Details about the work material and other requirements are written under this subheading. This should include the size, number of pieces or quantity, material specification, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tools required: A list of tools and equipment required for the practice is given under this subheading.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>List of operations: The operations to be carried out for making the model have to be given as a list, below the subheading.
5.5. Procedure: After completing the work on the model, the procedure followed for making the model has to be written in the second right page, using past tense and in third person. This should contain all details about operations, controls, safety measures, etc., related to the making of model.</p>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="6">
<li>Result: It is a custom to write the result of the practice as the last paragraph of the record. This includes the statement that whether the content of the aim is achieved or not by the practice.</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-755da9a7.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg">
FIGURE 2.2 Layout of work record/fair record for a practice.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-1d93c2b0.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-5-writing-of-the-fair-record">2.5 Writing of the Fair Record<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-5-writing-of-the-fair-record" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Fair record of a workshop study or practice is actually a fair copy of the work record, approved and signed by the instructor. As in the case of work record, the fair record should contain the following:</p>
<p>Study (as shown in Figure 2.1)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Right side pages</th><th>Left side pages</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Page 1 Heading, Serial. No. and date Aim Tools and equipment (list) Name and description of tools</td><td>Page 1 Sketches of tools and equipment</td></tr><tr><td>Page 2, 3, etc. Name &amp; description</td><td>Page 2, 3, etc. Sketches of tools and equipment</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Practice (as shown in Figure 2.2)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Right side pages</th><th>Left side pages</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Page 1 Heading, Serial. No. &amp; date Aim Work material Tools required List of operations</td><td>Page 1 Sketch of the model</td></tr><tr><td>Page 2 Procedure Result</td><td>Page 2 Sketch of the work material</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The fair record should be written in good handwriting. Corrections, over writing, etc., should be avoided. The main and subheading can be written using colour pen. The running matter has to be written using blue ink pen and the sketches using clutch pencil of HB lead. A fair record is the proof of the nature of the work done in the workshop and it has to be submitted at the time of examination for valuation. Hence, a student is advised to prepare the fair record in the most perfect manner to get the maximum benefit from it.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="exercises">EXERCISES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exercises" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="questions-for-viva-voce">Questions for Viva Voce<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions-for-viva-voce" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="answer-the-following-questions">Answer the following questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#answer-the-following-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-safety-measures">(A) Safety measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-safety-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Classify the types of safety measures to be taken in a workshop.</li>
<li>What is the preferred clothing, for a workshop practice? Why importance is given for this?</li>
<li>Explain the points to be considered for good housekeeping in a workshop.</li>
<li>What are the precautions to be taken while using hand tools in a workshop?</li>
<li>Describe the important safety measures to be followed, while operating machine tools.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-record-writing">(B) Record writing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-record-writing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>What are the materials to be possessed by a student as preparation for workshop practice?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain how a work-record for a study is written. Give the details regarding the writing of title and subtitles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe how a work-record for a practice is written. Give details.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How the procedure of doing a workshop model is written in a work-record?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What is the difference between work-record and fair record? Distinguish the salient features.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What are the subtitles to be contained in a fair record?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the important points to be considered while writing a fair record for a study as well as a model making practice.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Module B</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hand-working-processes">Hand Working Processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-working-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>3</p>
<p>Fitting</p>
<p>The term <em>fitting</em>, is related to assembly of parts, after bringing the dimension or shape to the required size or form, in order to secure the necessary fit. The operations required for the same are usually carried out on a work bench, hence the term <em>bench work</em> is also added with the name <em>fitting</em>.</p>
<p>As a part of the workshop practice, fitting process is studied by all engineering students. This gives the basic knowledge about engineering materials, cutting tools, measuring tools, different fitting operations, behaviour of metals, importance of geometry of shapes, etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-1-introduction-to-bench-work-and-fitting">3.1 Introduction to Bench Work and Fitting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-1-introduction-to-bench-work-and-fitting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fitting operations are generally done by using hand tools, after holding and placing the workpiece on a work bench. The tools and related equipment used for fitting processes can be classified as given below.</p>
<p>(a) Work holding devices:</p>
<ol>
<li>Work bench</li>
<li>Bench vice</li>
<li>Hand vice</li>
<li>V-block with clamp</li>
</ol>
<p>(b) Cutting tools:</p>
<ol>
<li>Files</li>
<li>Hack saws</li>
<li>Chisels</li>
<li>Hammers</li>
<li>Scrapers</li>
<li>Drills</li>
<li>Reamers</li>
<li>Tap and die</li>
<li>Drilling machine</li>
<li>Tool grinding machine</li>
</ol>
<p>(c) Measuring and marking tools:</p>
<ol>
<li>Surface plat</li>
<li>Engineer's try-square</li>
<li>Scribers</li>
<li>Punches</li>
<li>Steel rule</li>
<li>Vernier caliper</li>
<li>Outside and inside calipers</li>
<li>Dividers</li>
<li>Combination set</li>
<li>Micrometers</li>
<li>Vernier height gauge</li>
<li>Miscellaneous gauges</li>
</ol>
<p>(d) Tools for assembling and inspection:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Spanners</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pliers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Screw drivers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allen keys</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The operations done in fitting processes can be classified as given below:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Marking out</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hack sawing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chipping</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Filing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scraping</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drilling and reaming</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tapping and dieing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assembling</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-2-work-holding-devices">3.2 Work Holding Devices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-work-holding-devices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-2-1-work-bench">3.2.1 Work Bench<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-1-work-bench" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A fitting process can be done at various places, but most of the important operations of fitting are generally carried out on a table called work bench. The work bench is a strong, heavy and rigid table made up of hard wood. The size of the work bench required is about 150 to 180 cm length, nearly 90 cm width and approximately 76 to 84 cm height. Bench vice, is the device used to hold the workpiece and it is rigidly clamped on the top of the table as shown in Figure 3.1. Lockup drawers, to keep the tools used for fitting, are also usually provided below the table top.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-b2c2c372.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg">
FIGURE 3.1 Work bench with vice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-2-2-bench-vice">3.2.2 Bench Vice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-2-bench-vice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Bench vice is the most widely used device for holding the workpiece in position during various operations which are carried out in a fitting shop. It consists of one movable jaw and one fixed jaw as shown in Figure 3.2. The body of the vice is made up of iron or steel by casting. The threaded screw which is made to pass through the movable jaw at the outer end carries a handle at its end. Cast steel plates (known as jaw plates) are screwed to the jaw for holding the work rigidly. The gripping property of the jaw plates is increased by serrations provided with them. The base of the vice is bolted on the top of the work bench, nearby the edge.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ddf7b786.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg">
FIGURE 3.2 Bench vice.</p>
<p>A work is gripped between the parallel jaws by rotating the screw inside the nut, using the handle. The desired pressure is obtained by tightening or loosening the screw. In order to avoid the gripping marks on a finished surface of the workpiece, soft liners may be used on the jaw surfaces. The size of the vice is usually specified by the width of the jaws. The jaw size varies from 80 to 140 mm and the maximum opening ranges from 95 to 180 mm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-2-3-hand-vice">3.2.3 Hand Vice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-3-hand-vice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>For gripping small objects like screws, rivets, keys, etc., a hand vice is used. The commonly used type of hand vice is shown in Figure 3.3. It</p>
<p>basically consists of two steel legs hinged at the bottom and two jaws at the other ends. To keep the jaws separate, a leaf spring is provided nearby the hinged end. The jaws can be opened and closed by operating a wing nut and the screw.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-b4cdd12c.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg">
FIGURE 3.3 Hand vice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-2-4-v-block-with-clamp">3.2.4 V-block with Clamp<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-4-v-block-with-clamp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cylindrical objects can be clamped for drilling or similar operations by using a V-block and a U-clamp as shown in Figure 3.4. By keeping the round bar on the V-groove, the longitudinal axis of the bar coincides with that of the grove. This enables the marking of centre line, drilling of holes along the centre, etc., accurately.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-e68ea4b0.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg">
FIGURE 3.4 V-block with clamp.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-3-cutting-tools">3.3 Cutting Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-3-cutting-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-3-1-files">3.3.1 Files<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-3-1-files" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A file is a hardened piece of steel containing a high percentage of carbon or tungsten. Fine teeth are cut on the surface of the piece in slanting rows. Figure 3.5 shows the standard form of a file with wooden handle in detached position. The end called heal has a pointed portion called tong, which is used to fix the wooden handle. Files are classified according to the following factors:</p>
<ol>
<li>The cut and spacing of teeth on file.</li>
<li>The shape and form of the cross-section of file.</li>
<li>The length of file.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-719cabac.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg">
FIGURE 3.5 Parts of a file.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cut-and-spacing-of-teeth-on-file">Cut and spacing of teeth on file<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cut-and-spacing-of-teeth-on-file" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The teeth on a file may be of single cut or double cut. A single cut file will be having parallel teeth at <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>60</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">60^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> inclination to the centre line and is also known as flat files.
