<p>6</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="carpentry">Carpentry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carpentry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Carpentry is the process of shaping timber, using hand tools. The products produced are used in building construction, such as doors and windows, furniture manufacturing, patterns for moulding in foundries, etc. Carpentry work mainly involves the joining together of wooden pieces and finishing the surfaces after shaping them. Hence, the term <em>joining</em> is also used commonly for carpentry. A student studying the fundamentals of wood working has to know about timber and other carpentry materials, wood working tools, carpentry operations and the method of making common types of joints.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-materials-used-in-carpentry">6.1 Materials Used in Carpentry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-materials-used-in-carpentry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Basic materials used in carpentry shop are timber and plywood. Auxiliary materials used are nails, screws, adhesives, paints, varnishes, etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-1-timber">6.1.1 Timber<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-1-timber" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Timber is the name given to wood obtained from exogenous (outward growing) trees. In these trees, the growth is outward from the centre, by adding almost concentric layers of fresh wood every year known as <em>annual rings</em>. After the full growth, these trees are cut and sawed to convert into rectangular sections of various sizes for engineering purposes.</p>
<p>Timber is available in market in various shapes and size. The common shapes and sizes are given below:</p>
<ol>
<li><em>Log</em>: This is the trunk of the tree which is free from branches.</li>
<li><em>Balk</em>: This is the log after sawing roughly to square cross section.</li>
<li><em>Deal</em>: This is the log after sawing into rectangular cross section of width about 225 mm and thickness up to 100 mm.</li>
<li><em>Plank</em>: This is the timber piece having width more than 275 mm and thickness 50 to 150 mm.</li>
<li><em>Board</em>: This is the timber piece below 50 mm in thickness and above 125 mm in width.</li>
<li><em>Batten</em>: This is the timber piece below 175 mm in width and thickness between 30 mm to 50 mm in thickness.</li>
<li><em>Scantlings</em>: These are timber pieces of various assorted and nonstandard sizes other than the types given above.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-2-classification-of-wood">6.1.2 Classification of Wood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-2-classification-of-wood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The timber used for commercial purposes can be divided into two classes as <em>soft wood</em> and <em>hard wood</em>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="soft-wood">Soft wood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#soft-wood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A soft wood is light in weight and light coloured. They may have distinct annual rings but the medullary rays (radial lines) are not visible and the colour of the <em>sap wood</em> (outer layers) is not distinctive from the <em>heart wood</em> (inner layers). These woods cannot resist stresses developed across their fibres; hence, not suitable for wood working.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hard-wood">Hard wood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hard-wood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this type of wood the annual rings are compact and thin, and the medullary rays (radial lines) are visible in most cases Figure 6.1. Hard woods are nearly equally strong both along and across the fibres. Hard wood is the material used for wood working.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-31920de9.jpeg" alt="img-152.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.1 Cross-section of a hexogenous tree.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-3-indian-timber">6.1.3 Indian Timber<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-3-indian-timber" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of types of hard wood and soft wood available in India, which are suitable for carpentry work. Some of the popular names and a brief description of them are given below.</p>
<p><strong>Teak</strong>: This is a strong hard wood suitable for almost all important carpentry works. It has brown colour, is comparatively light in weight and easy to work. Shrinking during drying is little and can be easily seasoned. Highly finished and polished surfaces can give very good smoothness and appearance. Due to all these advantages, teak wood is commonly used for costly furniture, doors and windows. Teak is available in all over India and has small difference in material, properties and appearance from place to place.</p>
<p><strong>Sissu</strong>: This is a dark brown, tough and durable hard wood. It is considered as one of the best Indian woods suitable for furniture. This wood is available in northern and central India.</p>
<p><strong>Sal</strong>: This is a heavy, dark-coloured, close-grained hard wood. It is extensively used for building works as well as for railway spleepers. They grow abundantly in forests all over India. Seasoning of this wood is very slow and the wood working is hard.</p>
<p><strong>Mahogany</strong>: This is a hard wood having red brown colour. The grains are fine and have wavy shape. Since the wood contains resinous oil, insects cannot attack the wood. They are largely found growing in Himalayas. For pattern making and cabinet work, mahogany is very commonly used.</p>
<p><strong>Deodar</strong>: This is a light-coloured coarse grained wood used for carpentry work. Furniture, doors and windows, railway sleepers, etc. are built using this wood. They are seen in central and northern parts of India.</p>
<p><strong>Babul</strong>: This wood is pale red to brown in colour, hard and close-grained. It is used for making agricultural implements, body of carts, tool handles, etc. The wood grows all over India and is readily available for use.</p>
<p><strong>Mango</strong>: This is a soft wood of inferior quality. It can decay when exposed to wet weather and is affected by white ants. The wood is cheap and available all over India and used for making low cost doors, windows and furniture.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-4-plywood">6.1.4 Plywood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-4-plywood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Plywood is a thick sheet formed by pasting veneers of wood called <em>plys</em> together using glues. There will be three or more plys in a sheet and the grains of adjacent layers are kept at right angles to each other in order to get better strength in both directions. The outer layers are called <em>facing plys</em> and good hard wood veneers are used for that. The inner ones are called <em>core plys</em> and low quality wood is used for them. The plywood is made by either cold pressing or hot pressing.</p>
<p>Plywood can be used as solid board or stock which are having uniform thickness. Since the grains are oriented in perpendicular directions, plywood has better strength in both directions. It can be made in very large sheet size without joints. Plywood sheets can be bent to shapes of different designs. Decorative surfaces can be obtained by using costly attractive facing plys like teak wood. Due to the above advantages plywood sheets are very widely used for making furniture, boxes, doors, cupboards, etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-5-auxiliary-materials">6.1.5 Auxiliary Materials<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-5-auxiliary-materials" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of materials, other than timber, used in carpentry work. A brief description of them are given below:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Screws</strong>: Screws of different sizes and head forms are commonly used for fixing metallic fittings like hinges, tower bolts, etc. and for screwing parts strongly. They are made in steel or brass and is screwed to wood using screw drivers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bolts and nuts: To join heavy wooden parts, bolts and nuts of standard size are commonly used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nails: Wire nails having different head forms are used for reinforcing glued joints and fastening different parts. They may be made of brass, copper or mild steel.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dowels: A dowel is a wooden pin made out of bamboo or similar wood by the carpenter. It is used to secure wooden joints tightly by inserting through drilled holes across them.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Adhesives: To join parts having large area of surfaces, glues of different types are used. After applying the glue on the surface to be joined, the parts are kept in assembled position and secured tightly using clamps till drying or curing is complete. Some of the adhesives used in wood work are animal glue, casein glue, resin glue, vegetable glue, contact cement, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Surface coatings: After finishing the carpentry work, the surfaces of wooden parts are protected from moisture and weather by applying varnish, polish or oil paint. They can give better appearance also. French polish is the coating material commonly used for fine finished wooden parts. This consists essentially of shellac dissolved in methylated spirit. Synthetic enamel is the oil paint generally used to coat semi-finished wooden surfaces. A primer of this is applied initially, followed by enamel paint to get the finished surface.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-tools-for-wood-working">6.2 Tools for Wood Working<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-tools-for-wood-working" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of hand tools used in carpentry shops. They can be classified according to their uses mentioned below.</p>
<ol>
<li>Measuring and marking tools</li>
<li>Cutting tools</li>
<li>Striking tools</li>
<li>Planing tools</li>
<li>Work holding devices</li>
<li>Miscellaneous tools</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-1-measuring-and-marking-tools">6.2.1 Measuring and Marking Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-1-measuring-and-marking-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="rules">Rules<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rules" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>For measuring and setting out dimensions, various types of rules are used in carpentry shops. They include the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Steel rule: A stainless steel rule of length 30 cm or 60 cm.</li>
<li>Fourfold box-wood rule: This is a wooden scale consisting of four pieces joined together by hinges. The total length is usually 60 cm.</li>
<li>Flexible measuring rule: For measuring large dimensions as well as curved or angular surface dimensions, these tape type rules are used. When they are not in use, the tape is coiled into a small compact circular case.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="straight-edge-and-squares">Straight edge and squares<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#straight-edge-and-squares" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>To measure straightness as well as the perpendicularity of surfaces or edges, the following types of tools are used.</p>
<ol>
<li>Straight edge: This is a machined flat piece of wood or metal having perfectly straight and parallel edges.</li>
<li>Try square: This consists of a rectangular steel blade fixed rigidly to a hard wood stock or cast iron stock. The size varies from 150 to 300 mm according to the length of blade (Figure 6.2).</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-de529d1a.jpeg" alt="img-153.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.2 Try square.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Mitre square: For measuring 45°, a mitre square made of metal is used. The length of the blade is usually 200 to 300 mm.</li>
<li>Bevel square: For setting, duplicating, testing or comparing angles, a bevel square is used. It is similar to try square with a difference that the blade can be swivelled to any angle and fixed by screwing a wing nut.</li>
<li>Combination square: This is a combination of a square, 45° bevel, set square, rule, straight edge and centre finder, similar to the one used in fitting shops (Refer to Chapter 3).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scriber-or-marking-knife">Scriber or marking knife<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scriber-or-marking-knife" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To convert the pencil lines drawn on the wooden surface into deep scratch lines on the surface, the marking knife is used. They are made of steel with a sharp point at one end and a flat blade at the other end as shown in Figure 6.3(a).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gauges">Gauges<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gauges" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Gauges are used to mark lines parallel to the edge of a wooden piece. It mainly consists of a wooden stem sliding inside a wooden stock. The stem carries one or more steel marking points at one end. The stock position on the stem can be varied and fixed rigidly by tightening the thumb screw. To mark a line parallel to an edge, the gauge stock is held firmly against the edge and pushed along it, pressing the steel pointer to the surface. Depending on the purpose, the gauges can be grouped as mentioned below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Marking gauge: [Figure 6.3(b)] To mark single line.</li>
<li>Mortise gauge: To mark two parallel lines.</li>
<li>Cutting gauge: To cut thin section to get straight strips (up to 3 mm) instead of marking parallel to the edge.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-deb3dbb4.jpeg" alt="img-154.jpeg">
(a) Marking knife</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-34c7d24e.jpeg" alt="img-155.jpeg">
(b) Marking gauge
FIGURE 6.3 Marking tools.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="miscellaneous-measuring-tools">Miscellaneous measuring tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#miscellaneous-measuring-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In carpentry shops there are many measuring and marking tools other than the types explained above. Some of the frequently used tools are given below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Wing compass: It is used to mark circles, arcs etc.</li>
<li>Trammel: This is a beam compass to mark large size radius.</li>
<li>Divider: It is used to divide and mark dimensions.</li>
<li>Spirit level: It is used to check the horizontality of flat surfaces.</li>
<li>Plumb bob: It is used to check the verticality of a surface.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-2-cutting-tools">6.2.2 Cutting Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-2-cutting-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="saws">Saws<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#saws" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Saw is a cutting tool which has teeth on one edge and cutting is effected by reciprocating motion of the edge relative to the workpiece. There are different types of saws depending on the shape, size, use and direction of cutting motion. If the cutting occurs during the forward motion, such a saw is called push type, whereas in pull type the cutting occurs during backward motion. Commonly used types of saws are briefly explained below.</p>
<ol>
<li>Cross cut saw (Hand saw): It is used to cut thick wooden pieces across the grains (Figure 6.4). Cross cut saw has about 3 to 4 teeth per cm with a saw length of about 650 mm.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-655896a3.jpeg" alt="img-156.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.4 Cross cut saw.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Tenon saw (Back saw): This saw is used for short straight cuts (Figure 6.5). It has a parallel blade of 25 to 40 cm length and 6 to 10 cm width. The number of teeth per cm length ranges from 5 to 8. In order to avoid bending of blade during sawing, the blade is provided with a reinforcing strip at the top.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-c7182b56.jpeg" alt="img-157.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.5 Tenson saw.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Rip saw: It is a saw similar to hand saw used to cut wood along the grains.</li>
<li>Panel saw: This is similar to cross cut saw having finer blade and teeth, used for cutting panels of doors or similar pieces.</li>
<li>Compass saw: This is a saw having tapered blade which is narrow, long and flexible. It is used to cut along straight or curved lines.</li>
<li>Dove-tail saw: This is a saw of fine type like tenon saw, used to take fine and accurate cuts. The back side stiffener is provided in the saw.</li>
<li>Key hole saw (pad saw): This is the smallest type of saw used to cut key holes or the starting of any interior cut.</li>
<li>Bow saw: This saw has a narrow blade on a wooden frame of the shape of a bow. It is used to cut along sharp curves.</li>
<li>Coping saw: This saw has a narrow blade held in tension by a spring metal frame. It is used to cut small radius curves in thin wooden pieces.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chisels">Chisels<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chisels" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A large number of chisels are used in carpentry shops for cutting wood to get different desired shapes. The common types of chisels used are briefly explained below.</p>
<ol>
<li>Firmer chisel: They are the most common and general purpose chisel used by a carpenter [Figure 6.6(a)]. They have flat blade of about 15 to 50 mm width and 125 mm length.</li>
<li>Bevelled edge firmer (dove-tail) chisel: These chisels are used for fine and delicate works as well as for cutting corners [Figure 6.6(b)].</li>
<li>Mortise chisel: These chisels are used for heavy and deep cuts to remove a large quantity of wood. These chisels have width of about 15 mm, but the blade thickness may range from 6 to 15 mm [Figure 6.6(c)].</li>
<li>Gouges: These are chisels with curved sections. They are used to cut curved shapes of internal or external type.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-4f7a28d2.jpeg" alt="img-158.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.6 Chisels.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-2-3-striking-tools">6.2.3 Striking Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-3-striking-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Mallet: This is a wooden-headed hammer of round or rectangular cross section. The striking face is made flat as shown in Figure 6.7(a). Mallet is used for striking the cutting tools and has wooden handle.</li>
<li>Claw hammer: This is a hammer having steel head and wooden handle. The flat face of the head is used to drive nails and the claw portion for extracting nails out of the wood [Figure 6.7(b)].</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-23e1ae29.jpeg" alt="img-159.jpeg">
(a) Mallet</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-1b3be451.jpeg" alt="img-160.jpeg">
(b) Claw hammer</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-2-4-planing-tools">6.2.4 Planing Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-4-planing-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>To smoothen the flat wooden surfaces, planing tools are used. Depending on the size and construction and the surface finish obtained, planes are classified into the following categories.</p>
<ol>
<li>Wooden jack plane: This is the most commonly used plane in carpenters shops. The main part of a wooden jack plane is a wooden block called sole, to which a steel blade having knife edge is fixed at an angle with the help of a wooden wedge. The angle of the blade is kept about  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>45</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">45^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  to the bottom surface of the blade (Figure 6.8). The size of the blade is taken as 50 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>75</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">75\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">75</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span> . The knife edge of the blade is kept projecting 0.8 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1.6</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.6\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1.6</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  for roughing and  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.8</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.8\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0.8</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  to lower value for finishing.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d37fb6e8.jpeg" alt="img-161.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.8 Wooden jack plane.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Iron jack plane: In an iron jack plane the wooden sole is replaced by a cast iron channel-shaped body. A wooden knob in the front side and a wooden handle at the back side are fixed on the sole for pushing with two hands. The working principle is the same as that of wooden jack plane. Iron jack plane can give better finish, more life and fast stock removal, but the cost is higher than that of a wooden jack plane.</li>
<li>Smoothing plane: A smoothing plane is practically a wooden plane of smaller size, used for smoothening and finishing operations. Its length varies from 200 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>250</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">250\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">250</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
<li>Special planes: There are a number of types of planes used for special applications. A list of the important ones are given below:</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Trying plane: It is a large size plane to get fine flat surface.
(b) Rebate plane: It is used to make recess along the edge of a piece.
(c) Plough plane: It is used to make groove for fitting panels.
(d) Router plane: It is used to finish the bottom of a groove.
(e) Circular plane: It is used to smoothen circular surfaces.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-5-work-holding-devices">6.2.5 Work Holding Devices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-5-work-holding-devices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Work bench: This is a table of heavy size and rigid construction made of hard wood. The size ranges from 50 to 180 cm in length and about 90 cm in width. Two or four carpenters can work at a time on this work bench. Carpenter's vice and bench-hook are fixed on the edge and top respectively as shown in Figure 6.9.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d233d2c6.jpeg" alt="img-162.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.9 Work bench.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Carpenter's bench vice: The most common type of bench vice used in a carpentry shop is shown in Figure 6.10. It consists of a jaw fixed on the table side and a movable jaw kept in position by means of a screw and a handle. The body of vice is made of cast iron or steel. The jaws are lined with hard wood which can be renewed when it is damaged. The screw works inside a fixed half nut which can be engaged or disengaged by operating the lever. By pulling the lever the nut is disengaged from the screw allowing the jaw to move fast. When the lever is released, the nut engages and the screwing action is obtained.</li>
<li>Bench stop (hook): A bench stop or hook is a wooden block of shape as shown in Figure 6.11. This is placed on the edge of the work bench in order to prevent the workpiece moving forward, while planing or chiselling.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-24e223c8.jpeg" alt="img-163.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.10 Bench vice.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-c412c0c0.jpeg" alt="img-164.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.11 Bench hook.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Bench hold fast: The bench hold fast shown in Figure 6.12 is made up of steel and is used to hold the work piece on the table, while doing cutting or similar operations.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-07e12fff.jpeg" alt="img-165.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.12 Bench hold fast.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Sash (bar) cramp: This is made of a bar of steel, two jaws and a screw as shown in Figure 6.13. The work is clamped between jaws by rotating the screw using the handle. It is used for clamping glued pieces tightly or holding the workpieces of large size together for various operations.</li>
<li>C or G clamp: The clamp of the shape of letter C or G is used to clamp short pieces together as the bar cramp. Figure 6.14 shows a typical form of the clamp.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-6a39fd6a.jpeg" alt="img-166.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.13 Sash (Bar) cramp.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-a7e8ad3a.jpeg" alt="img-167.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.14 C or G clamp.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Hand screws: Figure 6.15 shows the general form of a hand screw. It is used for clamping or holding pieces tightly for various carpentry operations or pasting sheets together.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-7094ef61.jpeg" alt="img-168.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.15 Hand screw.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-6-miscellaneous-tools">6.2.6 Miscellaneous Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-6-miscellaneous-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of tools other than the types explained above, which are used in carpentry shops to meet the requirements. The frequently used tools of this group are given below.</p>
<ol>
<li>Rasps and files: Rasp is a rough file used to remove wood from the surface, corners, etc., resulting very rough surface. Ordinary files are used to smoothen such surfaces.</li>
<li>Sand paper: This is a thick paper coated with sharp-edged sand or glass particles of fine type on one side of it. When the sand paper is rubbed on the surface, a thin layer of wood is removed resulting smooth surface. The grades of them are denoted by numbers as 00, 1, etc.</li>
<li>Pincer: This is a tool similar to pliers and is used while screw is extracted from or driven into the wood.</li>
<li>Screw drivers: They are used to drive wood screw into or from the workpiece.</li>
<li>Hand drill: To make small size holes of less depth, hand drills are commonly used. Drill bits of suitable designs are used as the cutting tool. The hand drill can be of hand operated or electrically operated type.</li>
<li>Auger: For making large size deep holes of diameter from 8 mm to 25 mm, augers of suitable size and length are used in carpentry shops. It consists of a steel bar carrying a fluted body in the lower half and a rod on the upper half Figure 6.16. The bottom end of the fluted body is provided with a screw point, which acts as a pivot. Near the pilot screw, there are two cutting edges formed by the end of the twisted body. On the top end there is the wooden handle. To make a hole, the auger screw point is pressed to the wood and rotated with two hands slowly to drive it in like a screw and form the hole.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-93bd7d69.jpeg" alt="img-169.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.16 Auger.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Tools for sharpening: To sharpen chisels, oil stone is commonly used. For sharpening the saw tpeeth, triangular files are sufficient. The teeth are set (bending the alternate teeth on each side) using the tool called saw-set. This tool is basically a steel plate with gaps or gates of size equal to the thickness of the saw blade. By bending the teeth on both sides, the cutting slot become slightly wider than the thickness of blade, resulting in easy movement of saw.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-3-wood-working-processes">6.3 Wood Working Processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-3-wood-working-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The wood working processes usually practised for shaping the wood and making joints are the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Marking</li>
<li>Sawing</li>
<li>Planing</li>
<li>Chiselling</li>
<li>Mortising</li>
<li>Tenoning</li>
<li>Grooving and tongueing</li>
<li>Rebating</li>
<li>Recessing</li>
<li>Boring</li>
<li>Moulding</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="marking">Marking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The process of setting out dimensions on a rectangular block of wood is known as marking and laying out. Each dimension is set with the help of steel rule and different measuring as well as marking tools like try square, calliper, marking knife, marking gauge, etc. The wooden pieces should be planed to true rectangular cross section whenever necessary before marking. The marking may be required at several stages of the work, depending on the product shape.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sawing">Sawing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sawing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is the basic operation carried out for cutting the wood along the grains or across the grains to get different shapes. To start a cut, the thumb of the left hand is placed nearby the cutting line so that it steadies the blade, enabling to start the cut in the correct place. After one or two short movements, a groove is formed and then the full stroke is given. Light pressure has to be applied during rest of the cutting time, so that the blade is moving steadily for nearly its full length.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="planing">Planing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#planing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Planing is the process of making wood surface smooth and plane by removal of a small layer of wood from it. Planes of suitable type are to be used for that. Direction of the wood grains should be checked before starting the process and the planing has to be done along the grains. While planing, pressure is applied to each forward stroke which is released in the return stroke. Usually the plane is gripped in the right hand and the downward pressure as well as the forward movement are applied. The left hand is used to grip the front top portion of the plane for supporting the action. As the planing proceeds, the work piece should be checked for its flatness as well as squareness using a try square.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chiselling">Chiselling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chiselling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Chiselling is the process of removal of wood in very small quantities by cutting like scraping process, using a chisel alone after holding the chisel in the two hands. The workpiece is usually gripped on a vice or bench hold fast. To make the required shape from a wood piece, chiselling has to be done very carefully and in the proper way. The skill of chiselling has to be developed by practice. Some guidelines for better results are given below.</p>
<ol>
<li>To cut along horizontal plane, the chisel is held slightly tilted to one side and pushed forward in the direction of the grain. The bevel side is kept down for roughening, while for finishing, the straight side is kept down.</li>
<li>The handle of the chisel is slightly lowered down and chiselled from both sides to avoid splintering the edges and corners.</li>
<li>In vertical chiselling across the grains, the chisel is controlled with the left hand pressing firmly on the blade of the chisel.</li>
<li>The chisel is tilted slightly to one side to give a shearing cut.</li>
<li>While rounding a corner, the chiselling should start at the edge near the corner, keeping the direction of cutting towards the corner. This will avoid the biting of the chisel corner into the grain and splitting of the wood.</li>
</ol>
<p>For heavier cuts, firmer chisels are used and the cutting action is obtained by hitting the wooden mallet on the chisel handle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mortising">Mortising<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mortising" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A cavity or slot made in a wood piece is called mortise. The process of making a mortise is called mortising. To produce a mortise, firmer and mortise chisels are used. Mallet is used to strike over the chisel handle for heavier cuts. The wood is excavated from about half the depth of the cavity from one side and the other half from the opposite side. This can prevent the splitting of the wood on the surface, while making a mortice. Figure 6.17 shows three types of mortises generally used in carpentry joints.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-fcae4108.jpeg" alt="img-170.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.17 Types of mortises.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tenoning">Tenoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tenoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Tenon is the projection made on a wood piece to fit inside a mortise for getting a joint and the process of making the projection is called tenoning. The assembly is called a mortise and tenon joint, which is very commonly used in carpentry. A tenon saw is used to remove the excess wood to produce the tenon. The finishing of the tenon is done using chisel as explained earlier in chiselling. Figure 6.18 shows three types of tenons used in carpentry.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-0503c71f.jpeg" alt="img-171.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.18 Types of tenons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="grooving-and-tongueing">Grooving and tongueing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#grooving-and-tongueing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>To make wide planks, rectangular pieces have to be joined by taking groove on one edge and projection on the mating edge. The process of making a rectangular groove on a long edge is called <em>grooving</em> and the process of making a rectangular projection on the long edge to fit in the groove is called <em>tongueing</em>. Table tops, large size drawing boards, etc., are made like this. A groove is a channel cut along the long edge and a tongue is a corresponding projection to fit into the groove (Figure 6.19). The groove is cut with a plough plane and tongue with tongueing (or moulding) plane.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d4261eee.jpeg" alt="img-172.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.19 Groove and tongue of a joint.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rebating">Rebating<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rebating" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the process of making a rebate or undercut (step) along the edge of a piece of wood as shown in Figure 6.20. Rebates are used on door frames to fit the door panel or on window panel to fit the glass. Rebating is done using a rebating plane or plough plane. Chisel and mallet can also be used for cutting this.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-e99ae47f.jpeg" alt="img-173.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.20 Rebate on a piece.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="recessing">Recessing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recessing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the process of making a depression or recess along a wood piece as shown in Figure 6.21. It is actually a mortising operation in which the hole is blind and not much deep. Recessing is done using chisel and mallet as explained in mortising.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-e8a595a2.jpeg" alt="img-174.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.21 Recess on a piece.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="boring">Boring<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#boring" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The process of production of round through or blind holes is called <em>boring</em>. They are made using drills or augers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="moulding">Moulding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moulding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Curved projections or grooves along the length of piece of wood are made using moulding planes which has the cutter blade of the shape required. The process of making long grooves and projections by planing is called <em>moulding</em>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-4-carpentry-joints">6.4 Carpentry Joints<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-4-carpentry-joints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-5-wood-working-machines">6.5 Wood Working Machines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-5-wood-working-machines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wood working machines are commonly used in modern carpentry shops in addition to the hand tools explained earlier. The popular types of machines are listed below.</p>
<ol>
<li>Band saw</li>
<li>Circular saw</li>
<li>Wood working lathe</li>
<li>Wood planer</li>
<li>Mortiser</li>
<li>Sanding machines</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="band-saw">Band saw<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#band-saw" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Band saw is a machine designed to cut wood into blocks, planks, boards or battens. It has an endless metal saw band that travels over the rims of two or more rotating wheels. There are horizontal band saw for slicing heavy logs and vertical band saw for reslicing to small sections. Figures 6.27(a) and (b) show the principle of working of the two types of saws.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ed19427b.jpeg" alt="img-188.jpeg">
(a) Horizontal band saw</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-f9eb093d.jpeg" alt="img-189.jpeg">
(b) Vertical band saw</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-06058baa.jpeg" alt="img-190.jpeg">
(c) Circular saw</p>
<p>FIGURE 6.27 Types of machine saws.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="circular-saw">Circular saw<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#circular-saw" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Circular saw (also called table saw) basically consists of a rotating saw of the shape of a circular disc and a table on which it is fitted as shown in Figure 6.27(c). This saw is used for cross cutting as well as for small cutting operations like grooving, rebating, tenoning, bevelling, etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wood-working-lathe">Wood working lathe<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wood-working-lathe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wood working lathe is generally used in carpentry shops for turning jobs to produce cylindrical shapes. This machine is similar to a lathe used for turning metal in machine shops (Figure 6.28). It consists of a cast iron bed, a head stock to hold and give the rotational motion to the work at one end, a tail stock to support the work at the other end and a tool rest to feed the cutting tool relative to rotating work for cutting action.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-1ce4fc7a.jpeg" alt="img-191.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.28 Wood working lathe.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wood-planer">Wood planer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wood-planer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To plain large and heavy stocks, wood planers are used. The boards to be planed are fed by means of feed rolls along a table against a cutting head. A single surfacer machine has only one cutter head and cuts only from top side. The double surfacer carries two cutter heads on the top and bottom so that it can finish board surfaces by single pass through them. The capacity of a planner is designed by the maximum thickness and maximum width of stock that it can plane.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mortiser">Mortiser<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mortiser" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Motiser is a machine used to produce mortise on wooden pieces to make joints. There are three types of mortising machines.</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Hollow chisel mortiser</strong>: This machine has a revolving spindle which carries an auger bit which rotates at high speed inside a hollow chisel of square section. When the chisel is forced into the wood, the bits makes a square hole by the sharp end of the chisel. This machine is more popular.</li>
<li><strong>Chain mortiser</strong>: This machine has an endless chain which has saw teeth on its outer surface. This machine can make a long slot or hole having round bottom corresponding to the profile of the revolving chain.</li>
<li><strong>Oscillating bit mortiser</strong>: This machine carries an oscillating router bit and produces comparatively small mortises suitable for small cabinets.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sanding-machines">Sanding Machines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sanding-machines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To finish the machined wooden surfaces to the required smoothness, sanding machines are used. The type of sanding machines which are generally used in shops are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Belt sander</strong>: It uses an endless cloth backed abrasive belt running over two drums.</li>
<li><strong>Disc sander</strong>: It uses of a rotating disc of abrasive like grinding wheel for smoothening curved surfaces.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-6-carpentry-practice">6.6 Carpentry Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-6-carpentry-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example">Example<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Make a Tee (halved) joint of the dimensions given in Figure 6.29 using the given wood piece. The time allotted is 3 hours.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-14e5c72d.jpeg" alt="img-192.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.29 T-(Halved) joint.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim">Aim<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="work-material">Work material<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#work-material" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Material: Hard wood.</p>
<p>Size: Size 48 × 25 × 250 mm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tools-required">Tools required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Steel rule,</li>
<li>Try square,</li>
<li>Tenon saw,</li>
<li>Firmer chisel,</li>
<li>Mallet,</li>
<li>Jack plane,</li>
<li>Bench vice,</li>
<li>Bench hold fast,</li>
<li>Bench hook,</li>
<li>Marking gauge,</li>
<li>Scriber.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-of-operations">List of operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-of-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Marking,</li>
<li>Planing,</li>
<li>Sawing,</li>
<li>Chiselling.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Copy the given drawing in the work record.</li>
<li>Collect the tools and the wood piece.</li>
<li>Check the size of the wood piece for its suitability to make the model as per drawing.</li>
<li>Plane the wood piece to bring to the required cross section using jack plane. The geometrical accuracy is checked by using a try square.</li>
<li>Cut the wood piece into two using tenon saw and layout the dimensions of the model.</li>
<li>Remove the excess wood by saw cutting keeping a thin layer of wood for finishing the joining surfaces.</li>
<li>Finish the halved tee joint surfaces by chiselling as per dimensions and complete the model as shown in Figure 6.30.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-57c29159.jpeg" alt="img-193.jpeg">
FIGURE 6.30 T-(Halved) joint details.</p>
