<p>7</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="blacksmithy">Blacksmithy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blacksmithy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The process of shaping steel by hand hammering at red hot temperature, after placing on an anvil is called smithing. It is considered as one of the oldest methods of shaping metals.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-1-principle-of-smithing-and-forging">7.1 Principle of Smithing and Forging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-1-principle-of-smithing-and-forging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Smithing and machine forging are the metal-shaping processes. Smithing is used to shape relatively small jobs by hand hammering. Medium and large size components are shaped using machine forging process. In both cases the metal is heated to red hot temperature (i.e. above the recrystallization temperature) to make it soft and plastic. In smithing the heating is done in open fire or hearth while for machine forging the metal is heated in closed furnaces. In hand forging, hand tools and hammers are used to shape metal. The skill of the operator is the primary part to produce the required shape and dimensions.</p>
<p>A component made by hammering gives high strength to resist dynamic loads than that made by any other processes. Hence, forging process is the only one used to make parts like hooks, levers, cranks, connecting rods, spanners, hammers, hand tools, agricultural implements, etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-2-heating-equipment">7.2 Heating Equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-2-heating-equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The heating equipment used for smithing is called open hearth or smith's forge. Figure 7.1 shows a commonly used smith's forge. It basically consists of a robust cast iron or steel table on which the fuel (coke) is burned. Air at low pressure coming from a blower, is supplied to the fire place (hearth) through a nozzle called tuyere. A hood and a chimney are provided above the hearth to collect hot gases and fumes coming from the fire place. The hearth (the table top) and the vertical wall are lined with fire bricks to resist heat. The tuyere connected to the pipeline supplying low-pressure air, is regulated by a valve. A small water tank is provided around the tuyere (at the back of the wall) to cool it. For quenching and cooling of the workpiece and tools, a small water tank of rectangle shape is also provided on the front side of the hearth.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-009f49ca.jpeg" alt="img-198.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.1 Smith's forge or hearth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-3-tools-and-appliances">7.3 Tools and Appliances<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-tools-and-appliances" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The types of tools and appliances used commonly for smithing are given below:</p>
<p>(a) Work supporting tools
(b) Hammers
(c) Tongs
(d) Metal shaping tools
(e) Measuring tools</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-3-1-work-supporting-tools">7.3.1 Work Supporting Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-1-work-supporting-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anvil">Anvil<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anvil" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Anvil is used to support the workpiece while it is being struck with hammer (Figure 7.2). The body of anvil is made of cast steel or wrought iron with hardened plate welded to the top. The horn or beak is used to bend or form curved shapes. The commonly used size of anvil is of 150 kg. The anvil is supported by an iron stand.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ea651147.jpeg" alt="img-199.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.2 Anvil.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="swage-block">Swage block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#swage-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a heavy block of cast steel or cast iron with a number of slots and holes of different shapes (Figure 7.3). It is used to support in punching holes and forming different shapes.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-52f9eb1d.jpeg" alt="img-200.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.3 Swage block. Bick iron</p>
<p>This is a small anvil which can support workpieces of small size for smithing operations. The bick iron is made of tool steel and the shank of it is fitted with the hardie hole of anvil while in use (Figure 7.4).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-891d93b1.jpeg" alt="img-201.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.4 Bick iron.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-3-2-hammers">7.3.2 Hammers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-2-hammers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Different types of hammers are used to apply blow directly on the metal or on the shaping tools (Figure 7.5). The eye hole of the hammer is normally made to oval shape and accommodates the handle of wood or bamboo. The weight of a hammer used varies from 1 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>2</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2\mathrm{kg}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">kg</span></span></span></span></span></span>  for peen hammers and 2 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>8</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">8\mathrm{kg}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">8</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">kg</span></span></span></span></span></span>  for sledge hammers.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-3c6e5f0d.jpeg" alt="img-202.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-a2ea19db.jpeg" alt="img-203.jpeg">
(a) Ball peen</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-dd7ae078.jpeg" alt="img-204.jpeg">
(b) Cross peen</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-0ff130f9.jpeg" alt="img-205.jpeg">
(c) Straight peen</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-f377b2c1.jpeg" alt="img-206.jpeg">
(d) Sledge</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-3-3-tongs">7.3.3 Tongs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-3-tongs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>To grip and turn hot workpieces, different types of holding tools called tongs are used (Figure 7.6). A tong consists of two bars jointed by a rivet or a pin. The total length of a tong varies from 450 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>650</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">650\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">650</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span> . Different shapes are given to the mouth of the tong in order to hold jobs of different forms.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ac12149b.jpeg" alt="img-207.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.5 Types of hand hammers.
(a) Flat tong</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ed4195d6.jpeg" alt="img-208.jpeg">
(b) Side bit tong</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-614b391d.jpeg" alt="img-209.jpeg">
(c) Round hollow tong</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-e89dac04.jpeg" alt="img-210.jpeg">
(d) Square hollow tong</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-83834851.jpeg" alt="img-211.jpeg">
(e) Pickup tong
FIGURE 7.6 Smith's tongs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-3-4-metal-shaping-tools">7.3.4 Metal Shaping Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-4-metal-shaping-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Tools like fullers swages, chisels, etc., are used to shape hot metal (Figure 7.7). These tools are placed over the area to be shaped and blows are applied over them using hammers. The shaping tools are made of high carbon steel in different sizes to suit the various types of jobs.</p>
<ol>
<li>Fuller: It is used to make necks and drawing out a section.</li>
<li>Swage: It is used to reduce and shape circular jobs.</li>
<li>Flatter: It is used to level and finish flat surfaces.</li>
<li>Set hammer: It is used to level and finish corners of flat surfaces.</li>
<li>Chisel: It is used to cut metal in hot and cold state.</li>
<li>Punch: It is used to produce hole in hot state.</li>
<li>Drift: It is used to expand the size of a hole after punching.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-944617d0.jpeg" alt="img-212.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.7 Metal shaping tools.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-3-5-measuring-tools">7.3.5 Measuring Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-5-measuring-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Simple measuring tools are used during smithing operations. The dimension or shape of a hot workpiece has to be inspected between forging operations and after finishing. The following are the measuring instruments usually required in smithy.</p>
<ol>
<li>Steel rule of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>30</mn><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30~\mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">30</span><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  or  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>60</mn><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">60~\mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">60</span><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  length</li>
<li>Outside and inside callipers</li>
<li>Gauges</li>
<li>Templates</li>
</ol>
<p>These tools are explained with figures in Chapter 3.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-4-heating-of-metal">7.4 Heating of Metal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-4-heating-of-metal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Various types of steels such as mild steel, carbon steel, structural steel and tool steels are the common raw materials for forging. Nonferrous metals and alloys like brass, bronze, copper and aluminium can also be forged. The temperature ranges for forging steels are given below:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Material</th><th>Forging temp. in ( {}^{\circ} \mathrm{C} )</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Mild steel</td><td>750-1300</td></tr><tr><td>Medium carbon steel</td><td>750-1250</td></tr><tr><td>High carbon steels and alloys</td><td>800-1150</td></tr><tr><td>Stainless steels</td><td>940-1180</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>For smithing the temperature of steel is estimated by the colour of the heated zone. Dark red colour is obtained at about  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>700</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">700^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">70</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>  and cherry red at  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>900</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">900^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">90</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> . The colour becomes orange at  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>1100</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1100^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">110</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>  and white hot at  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>1300</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1300^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">130</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span> .</p>
<p>Heating of steel improves softness and reduces tensile strength resulting its plasticity and malleability. Proper heating gives easiness for shaping of metal and good surface finish. If the metal is overheated and kept for long time in a furnace, burning due to oxidation may occur resulting cracks on surface or melting of the heat-effected zone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-forging-operations">7.5 Forging Operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-forging-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A given metal piece (blank) can be converted to the required shape by one or more of the following forging operations.</p>
<ol>
<li>Upsetting or Jumping</li>
<li>Drawing out or drawing down</li>
</ol>
<p>(i) Fullering
(ii) Swaging</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Punching and drifting</li>
<li>Bending and twisting</li>
<li>Setting and finishing.</li>
<li>Cutting.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-1-upsetting-or-jumping">7.5.1 Upsetting or Jumping<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-1-upsetting-or-jumping" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Upsetting, jumping or heading is a process of forging in which the cross section of the workpiece is increased by reducing its length. The heated metal piece is kept vertical over the anvil with the help of tongs and blows are given at the end, so that the hot portion swells to increase its dimension (Figure 7.8). Initially the bar stock will be of a round or</p>
<p>square uniform section. Different cross sections larger than the bar stock are produced by this upsetting operation.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-c47aaeae.jpeg" alt="img-213.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.8 Upset forging operations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-2-drawing-out-or-drawing-down">7.5.2 Drawing Out or Drawing Down<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-2-drawing-out-or-drawing-down" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a process of reducing the cross section of the workpiece and hence is the reverse of upsetting. Fullering and swaging are the two basic types of drawing processes (Figure 7.9). In fullering, the rectangular cross sections are reduced in thickness and the length of the portion increases proportionally. Fullering can also be used to increase width of the portion. If a round portion is to be drawn, swages are used for that and the operation is called swaging. To get a round cross section of smaller diameter form a bar stock of square section, the portion is first converted to octagon and then to round using swages.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d7f32293.jpeg" alt="img-214.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-61336dba.jpeg" alt="img-215.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-65486de8.jpeg" alt="img-216.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d3b25386.jpeg" alt="img-217.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.9 Drawing out or drawing down operations.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-681cd41f.jpeg" alt="img-218.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-3-punching-and-drifting">7.5.3 Punching and Drifting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-3-punching-and-drifting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Punching is a process of forcing a punch through hot metal to produce a hole. To make a hole in hot metal piece, it is placed over the anvil flat and the punch is forced to half of thickness (Figure 7.10). Then the job is turned upside down and placed over a bolster having a hole on the prithel hole of anvil. The punch is forced again to get the hole. In order to increase to punch hole size, a drift (tool like a punch) is forced through the hole and the process is named drifting.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-79c79e6c.jpeg" alt="img-219.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-5856632f.jpeg" alt="img-220.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.10 Punching.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-4-bending-and-twisting">7.5.4 Bending and Twisting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-4-bending-and-twisting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>With the help of anvil horn or bick iron, bars, flats, strips, wires, etc., can be bent by hammering. Similarly twisting of flat strips can be done by using tongs and a rectangular hole or vice as given in Figure 7.11.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-2cac759d.jpeg" alt="img-221.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-f4ae9c53.jpeg" alt="img-222.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.11 Bending.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-5-setting-down-and-finishing">7.5.5 Setting Down and Finishing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-5-setting-down-and-finishing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Setting down is a process of making the round corners to square shape by the use of set hammer (Figure 7.12). Even though a set hammer is the form of a sledge hammer with square corners, it is not used for applying blows. It is used just like a fuller to correct the corners. Finishing is the operation of running unevenness of surfaces by the use of flat fuller or set hammer. Roughly-shaped round surfaces are converted to finished form by using swages.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-eb972132.jpeg" alt="img-223.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.12 Setting down.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-5-6-cutting">7.5.6 Cutting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-6-cutting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Metal in hot or cold condition is cut by using chisels. This operation is used to remove excess metal from a job or to split a part or to make pieces from a long bar stock Refer (Figure 7.13).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-f77df07f.jpeg" alt="img-224.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.13 Cutting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-6-smithing-practice">7.6 Smithing Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-6-smithing-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In smithing, the metal piece heated to the forging temperature is placed in position on anvil using a tong in left hand and is struck by a hammer holding in right hand. Usually a helper is also required for making complicated shapes. In such cases, the operator holds the workpiece with his left hand and places the shaping tool like fuller swage, etc., in right hand. The helper strikes on the shaping tool with sledge hammer in both hands.</p>
<p>The skill of the operator plays major part in producing finished forgings. The number of heatings (passes) may be six or more, but a skilled person requires minimum number of reheating.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-6-1-smithing-procedure">7.6.1 Smithing Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-6-1-smithing-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The steps to be followed to produce a component by smithing are given below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Study the drawing of the component to be forged and calculate the approximate volume of metal required.</li>
<li>Take a blank of shape suitable to the component, having a total volume of at least 5 to 10% excess. The excess volume is provided for losses due to scaling and trimming.</li>
<li>Plan the forging operations and the sequence. Prepare an operation process chart in detail.</li>
<li>Collect the forging and measuring tools and keep them ready for use.</li>
<li>Place the blank in the hearth for heating as specified in the process chart.</li>
<li>Check the temperature of the metal by its colour and take it out, when it reaches the forging temperature using proper shape of tongs.</li>
<li>Do the forging operations one by one without delay. If the temperature becomes low, keep it for re-heating.</li>
<li>Repeat the above steps several times, till the shape and size of component reaches the required one.</li>
<li>Quench the workpiece in water to bring it to room temperature and do the final inspection.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-6-2-safety-measures">7.6.2 Safety Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-6-2-safety-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Use only the tongs, whose jaws fit the shape of the forging.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>See that the hammers are always securely attached to their handles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clean the hot stock and anvil from scales using steel brush or scraper.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Never attempt to forge cold or burnt metal.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wear proper uniform and shoes as specified by the shop rules.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hold the hot metal downward close to the ground, while handling it from forge (hearth) to the anvil.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Never keep any hot or cold forgings or waste materials to accumulate around the working place. They should be kept in proper storage locations.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example">Example<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Make a hexagonal chisel of the size shown in Figure 7.14 using the given cylindrical iron piece of diameter 25 mm and length 100 mm.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-31091cb0.jpeg" alt="img-225.jpeg">
FIGURE 7.14 Hexagonal chisel.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim">Aim<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To make a hexagonal chisel of given dimensions using the given cylindrical iron piece.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="materials-required">Materials required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#materials-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cylindrical iron piece of diameter 25 mm and length 100 mm and coke for heating.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tools-required">Tools required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Hammer, 2. Tongs, 3. Flatter, 4. Anvil, 5. Forge, and 6. Steel rule.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-of-operations">List of operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-of-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Heating, 2. Hammering to hexagonal prism, 3. Jumping to reduce length, 4. Hammering to shape conical end and 5. Hammering to shape chisel end.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Heat the given cylindrical piece to red hot temperature using the forge.</li>
<li>Take the heated piece using tongs and hammer it after placing lengthwise over the face of the anvil to form hexagonal prism.</li>
<li>Reduce the length of the prism to 100 mm by jumping, after holding it vertical over the anvil face.</li>
<li>Flatten the six faces using the flatter and finish the hexagonal shape.</li>
<li>Shape one end to conical form by hammering.</li>
<li>The other end is shaped to chisel form as shown in figure by hammering on the parallel flat faces, after keeping it on the anvil.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="exercises">EXERCISES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exercises" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="questions-for-viva-voce">Questions for Viva Voce<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions-for-viva-voce" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
