<ol>
<li>Coupler (coupling): Two pipe lines of equal diameter and in axial alignment can be joined by a coupler (coupling). It is a short sleeve with internal thread.</li>
<li>Reducer coupler (Reducer coupling): This is a coupler to join two pipe lines of different diameters in axial alignment.</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>90</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">9</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  Elbow: This is a pipe special used for effecting abrupt change in direction through  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>90</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">9</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> . Internal threads are provided on both ends. An elbow brings twice the head loss than a bend.</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>90</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">9</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  Reducer elbow: This is an elbow with outlet diameter less than that of inlet diameter. It is used to join two pipe lines having different diameters and meeting at right angle.</li>
<li>Bend: This is a pipe special used to effect gradual change in direction (usually  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>90</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">9</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> ). The two ends of the bend are externally threaded.</li>
<li>Return bend: This bend is used to return the direction of pipe line through  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>180</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">180^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">18</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> . The ends are internally threaded for fitting the pipe lines.</li>
<li>Tee: This pipe special is used to make a branch connection of same diameter to the main pipe line at right angle. A Tee is internally threaded and it connects three ends of pipes.</li>
<li>Reducer Tee: This is a pipe special similar to Tee used to take a branch connection of reduced diameter from the main pipe line.</li>
<li>Cross: This pipe special is used to take two branch connections at right angles to the main pipe line. The threads are provided internally.</li>
<li>Close nipple: A nipple is a short straight piece of pipe with external thread on both ends. A close nipple is the shortest one of this category with external thread for the full length. They are used to join two internally threaded pipe specials and valves.</li>
<li>Short nipple: A short nipple has the same shape and function of a close nipple, but it has a short unthreaded portion at the middle of its length for gripping.</li>
<li>Short nipple with hexagonal grip: This nipple has an additional hexagonal nut shape at the middle portion for easy screwing with spanner. It is similar to an ordinary short nipple, except that difference.</li>
<li>Hose nipple: A hose nipple is used to connect a hose (flexible pipe-usually plastic or rubber) to a pipe line. One end of the hose-nipple has a stepped taper to fit the hose, while other end has thread. A hexagonal</li>
</ol>
<p>nut shape is given to the middle portion for gripping with a spanner.</p>
<ol start="14">
<li><strong>Male plug:</strong> A male plug is used to close an internally threaded end of a pipe line or pipe special. It has external thread and a grip of square shape at the end.</li>
<li><strong>Female plug (cap):</strong> A female plug is used to close an externally thread end of a pipe or pipe special. It has internal thread and a grip of square shape at the end.</li>
<li><strong>Screwed union:</strong> It consists of three pieces as shown in the drawing. The two end pieces have internal threads at their ends which are connected to the pipe ends. The central hexagonal (or octagonal) piece (union nut) has internal thread at one end and a collar at the other end. After the end pieces are screwed on to the pipes, the central piece (union nut) is tightened to draw the end pieces together to get a water tight joint.</li>
<li><strong>Flange:</strong> This is a disc type pipe special having threaded hole at the centre for screwing to the externally threaded end of a pipe line. It will have holes around the central hole at equal angular spacing (3, 4, 6, or 8 Nos.) for joining to another similar flange or flat surface using bolt or stud. Example for the use of various pipe fittings in pipe line is given in Figure 9.2.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-fb4289e3.jpeg" alt="img-279.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.2 Use of pipe fittings.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-4-valves-and-meters">9.4 Valves and Meters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-4-valves-and-meters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Valves are used in piping systems to control or stop the flow of liquid or gas. The most common types of valves used in low pressure water pipe line are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Water tap</li>
<li>Water cock</li>
<li>Globe valve</li>
<li>Gate valve</li>
<li>Ball valve</li>
<li>Non-return valve</li>
<li>Foot valve</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water-tap">Water tap<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-tap" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To collect water from low pressure pipe line, water tap (screw-down valve) is commonly used. Figure 9.3 gives the cross section of the tap. Its leather or rubber faced valve disc is lifted or lowered by rotating the spindle. Brass or gun-metal is the material used for the valve body and the size is specified by the pipe to which it is fitted, usually ranging from 10 mm to 25 mm.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d89cc2fe.jpeg" alt="img-280.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.3 Water tap.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="water-cock">Water cock<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-cock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the simplest and smallest form of a valve in which a conical plug called cock is inserted into a conical hole having a matching taper. A rectangular hole is provided at the centre across the conical portion so that, in one position it permits flow of water as shown in Figure 9.4. A half turn of the handle will bring the solid portion of the cock to the water ways preventing the flow. Cocks are used for low rate of water flow or for tapping pressure line to a manometer etc.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-b6a2451a.jpeg" alt="img-281.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.4 Water cock.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="globe-valve">Globe valve<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#globe-valve" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Globe valves are used as control valves in fluid (gas and liquid) pipe lines. Figure 9.5 shows the simplest and smallest type of globe valve used in water pipe lines. Basically, the valve is a variable opening flow device. The design of a globe valve also creates a slight retardation to the flow because the fluid is forced to make a double turn and passes through the opening at 90° to the axis of the pipe. The valve plug is raised or lowered to stop or regulate the flow through a circular opening. A globe valve can be identified by the spherical body and the arrow mark for the direction of flow. These valves are used in water pipe lines from 12 mm to 100 mm or even larger diameter for the flow control purpose.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-3b0dca20.jpeg" alt="img-282.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.5 Globe valve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gate-valve">Gate valve<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gate-valve" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A gate valve is on-off type valve. It allows a straight-line movement of fluid and offer very little resistance to the flow in fully opened position. The central disc moves completely out of the passage and leaves a full opening. Figure 9.6 shows a simple type of gate valve partially opened in position. These valves are very widely used in water pipe lines of diameter ranging from 12 mm to higher values. A gate valve can be identified by its slim body. It is to be noted that there will be no arrow mark or the body of valve because it can be used in both ways.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-7d273f8d.jpeg" alt="img-283.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.6 Gate valve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ball-valve">Ball valve<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ball-valve" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A ball valve has a spherical shaped rotating part with a hole at the centre to on or off the flow through the pipe line. Figure 9.7 shows the assembly of the valve, top half in section. The ball is connected to a spindle and the spindle is turned to 90° with the help of a handle (lever) to on or off position. The external surface of the ball is made smooth and it rotates rubbing two PVC washers. The gland packing arrangement stops the leakage. Ball valve can be used as gate valve in pipe lines and offers minimum head loss.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-d58092bd.jpeg" alt="img-284.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.7 Ball valve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="non-return-valve">Non-return valve<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-return-valve" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the fluid flow in the reverse direction is to be stopped automatically in a pipe line, a non-return valve has to be fitted in the line. A type of non-return valve used pipe lines is shown in Figure 9.8. In this valve, the disc-valve portion at the centre is lifted when the pressure of water in the inlet side is greater than that of the outlet side, allowing the forward flow. When the pressure of outlet side exceeds that of inlet, the valve closes automatically stopping the reverse flow.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-5b38c036.jpeg" alt="img-285.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.8 Non-return valve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foot-valve">Foot valve<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foot-valve" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Foot valve is a kind of non-return valve used in centrifugal pumps. It is fitted at the bottom most end of the suction pipe (Foot) to stop flow in the downward direction for priming purpose. The strainer restricts the entry of floating materials to the pipe line. Figure 9.9 gives the details of the foot valve. The material used may be cast iron, brass, or PVC.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ffa7c980.jpeg" alt="img-286.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.9 Foot valve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water-meter">Water meter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-meter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water meter is one of the most common type of measuring device used in pipe lines for the measurement of volume of water flowing through it. Figure 9.10 shows the principle of working of a rotary type water meter. When water flows across the meter, the flow takes place in a helical path due to the inclined holes. As a result the propeller rotates operating a series of gears. The volume of water flowing through the meter can be directly read from the calibrated circular dial by noting the initial and final readings. The meter reading can be corrected by adjusting the position of the by pass control screw provided in the inlet side of the meter. Water meter is fitted at the entry point of water pipe line to a house or usage area.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-a0ef4d8c.jpeg" alt="img-287.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.10 Water meter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-5-plumping-fixtures-sanitary-fittings">9.5 Plumping Fixtures (Sanitary fittings)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-5-plumping-fixtures-sanitary-fittings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fixtures used in a building for receiving excreta and waste water</p>
<p>discharged by the users are called sanitary fittings. They include water closets, wash basins, kitchen sinks, bath tubs, flushing cisterns, shower stall, urinal, floor traps, etc.</p>
<p>Sanitary fixtures are connected to drain pipes of large diameter ranging from 50 mm to 100 mm. In modern types fittings PVC pipes are preferred, although asbestos pipes were the old practice. In order to prevent the reverse flow of foul air or gas through drainage pipes, traps are generally fitted after a fixture before connecting to the outlet pipe. A trap is a water seal with full of water. This collection is formed by a depression or bent fitting in the pipe line as shown in Figure 9.11. The traps can be classified according to the shape of them as P-trap, S-trap, and Q-trap.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-a361a38f.jpeg" alt="img-288.jpeg">
(a) P-Trap</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-1d043438.jpeg" alt="img-289.jpeg">
(b) Q-Trap</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-3cb78ad6.jpeg" alt="img-290.jpeg">
(c) S-Trap
FIGURE 9.11 Types of traps.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water-closets">Water closets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-closets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water closets (WC) are fixtures those receive and dispose off human excreta using water as the medium of conveyance.</p>
<p>There are three types of water closets:</p>
<ol>
<li>European (Pedestal or western) type WC</li>
<li>Indian (Squatting or oriental) type WC</li>
<li>Universal (Anglo-Indian) type WC</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="european-pedestal-or-western-type-wc">European (Pedestal or western) type WC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#european-pedestal-or-western-type-wc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This fixture has a bowel form, with oval shaped opening at the top, having 400 mm height to form a chair like structure. S-type or P-type trap is used according to the outlet pipe position. Figure 9.12 gives cross-section of a European WC.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ccfd4cd6.jpeg" alt="img-291.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-24ca5fe1.jpeg" alt="img-292.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.12 Water closet (Pedestal or western).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indian-squatting-or-oriental-type-wc">Indian (Squatting or oriental) type WC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indian-squatting-or-oriental-type-wc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These closets are installed at the floor level and enables a person to use it in a squatting position. Figure 9.13 gives cross-section of an Indian WC. Here, P type trap is used.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-97ad26b8.jpeg" alt="img-293.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-b9ca069c.jpeg" alt="img-294.jpeg">
Plan
FIGURE 9.13 Water closet (Squatting or oriental).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="universal-anglo-indian-type-wc">Universal (Anglo-Indian) type WC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#universal-anglo-indian-type-wc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a combination of the above two. The top is wider and the user can either sit as a European WC using the plastic seat, or squat on it as on an Indian one.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="flushing-systems">Flushing systems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#flushing-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water closets are flushed by discharging water through a suitable mechanism. Water of about 5 litres to 12.5 litres is to be delivered quickly (8–9s) i.e., at a rate of 1.5 l/s. Flush tanks (Flushing cisterns) placed above the WC gives the pressure (head) for efficient flushing. About 1.8 m is the best preferred head for better action. An inverted bell with a mechanism to lift it by a lever is installed above the flush. Siphonic cisterns operate only when the cistern is full of water. Hence, it does not waste water by overflow. Flush tanks are also available with 'beta valve' or similar mechanism which has direct opening from the flush tank and not through the siphon mechanism. This may bring over flow, if the valve is not perfectly working. A float-valve mechanism fitted at the water inlet point of the flush tank stops the inward flow when the tank is full. Flush valves are also available as substitute for flush tanks. They are mechanical valves fitted directly on the pipe line. Here, filling time is not required, so immediate flushing is possible after the previous one. This type is good for public toilets, where continuous use is there.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wash-basins-and-kitchen-sinks">Wash basins and kitchen sinks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wash-basins-and-kitchen-sinks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wash basins (Figure 9.14) used in lavatories are fitted with cold and hot water supply taps with mixing fixture. The waste collected by the basin is disposed using 32 mm diameter waste pipe. An additional stopcock (usually angle valve) is provided at the inlet of each tap to isolate the fixture when required. Basins are usually made up of porcelain-ware or plastic. Kitchen sinks are similar to the wash basins but the shape and dimensions are given suitable to kitchen use. Stainless steel is the material commonly used for the sink. The waste pipe fitted is of 40 or 50 mm diameter in order to facilitate disposal of small amount of solid waste.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-bbfbcc3c.jpeg" alt="img-295.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.14 Wash basin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bath-tubs-and-showers">Bath tubs and showers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bath-tubs-and-showers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Bath tubs are vessels capable of holding water and allowing a person to soak in, clean and relax. Hot and cold water is supplied and mixed in the tub for use. The water holding capacity of a standard tub is about 200 litres to 225 litres and the requirement of water is about 150 litres to 180 litres. Showers are provided for a spray of water which enables a person to wash himself while standing. The control valve is fitted for hot and cold water mixing at a convenient height.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="geysers">Geysers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geysers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Geyser is the name of hot water springs found in many parts of the world. This term is adopted for the appliance used for hot water supply unit in buildings. Electrically heated individual geysers are popular in India. It mainly contains a heating element wound around the pipe carrying water. When the electric supply is given, it heats the water flowing though it. The whole unit is of cylindrical shape and fitted in the bath room at overhead position to collect water. Centralized hot water supply system is used in hotels and flats to overcome cold season. The heating is done with the help of a boiler using electricity, gas or different types of fuels and the distribution is done through insulated pipelines.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-6-sketching-of-piping-layouts">9.6 Sketching of Piping Layouts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-6-sketching-of-piping-layouts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A neat line sketch of the piping layout is prepared before starting the plumbing process so that clear information about the layout of fixture, its connections, operating directions, etc. will be clear to all involved in the work.</p>
<p>Piping layout drawings can be classified as:</p>
<ol>
<li>Double line pictorial layout</li>
<li>Single line pictorial layout</li>
<li>Double line orthographic layout</li>
<li>Single line orthographic layout</li>
<li>Single line developed layout</li>
</ol>
<p>In double line piping layout all the pipes are represented by two lines and fittings are shown as it is seen. In single line layouts the pipes are shown by single thick line and the fittings by its symbols. In pictorial (Isometric) layouts, a three dimensional pictorial view is drawn. Figure 9.15 gives the example for the five types of piping layouts. Among the five types of layouts the single line isometric layout is the simplest and most suitable for sketching.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-58b1a536.jpeg" alt="img-296.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.15 Types of piping layouts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="representation-of-pipe-fittings-valves-and-fixtures">Representation of pipe fittings, valves and fixtures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#representation-of-pipe-fittings-valves-and-fixtures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The pipe fittings and valves of screwed type can be represented in piping layouts by graphic symbols. In an isometric view, there are three equal faces as shown in Figure 9.16. In isometric piping layout, the graphic symbols are to be shown in all three faces according to the requirement. Figure 9.17 shows a plumbing setup drawn using isometric graphic symbols. Figure 9.18 gives a list of graphic symbols for common pipe specials, drawn as on the right isometric face. It is to be noted that for screwed joints, say for an elbow, two short lines are shown to represent the ends. For a flanged joint, two parallel short lines are shown to represent the flanges. Figure 9.19 shows the graphic symbols for common types of valves. To show the various fixtures other than the pipe specials and valves, simplified forms of the equipment itself may be drawn.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-1b734cc4.jpeg" alt="img-297.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.16 Principle of Isometric view.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-fa274112.jpeg" alt="img-298.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.17 Sample of plumbing layout.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Description</th><th>Isometric symbol (right face)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td>Coupler</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Reducer coupler</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>90° Elbow</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Tee</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Cross</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>Bend</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>Plug (female)</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>Plug (male)</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>Union</td><td>↑</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>Hose nipple</td><td>↑</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>FIGURE 9.18 Isometric graphic symbols for pipe fittings.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Description</th><th>Isometric symbol (right face)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td>Gate valve</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Globe valve</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Water tap</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Water cock</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>FIGURE 9.19 Isometric graphic symbols for valve.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-7-water-supply-system">9.7 Water Supply System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-7-water-supply-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water supply system of different types are in use according to the area of application as residences, hostels, hospitals, industries, swimming pools, fire fighting, gardening, etc. The quantity of water required (per day, per person), the quality, pressure, temperature, etc., are also different. An expert plumber should gather clear idea about such things. In residences, the requirement is considered as 135 litres (90 for domestic purposes and 45 for flushing) per day per person. Data about such things are available from tables given in building code of practice. Figure 9.19 gives a sample of the layout of water supply used in a multiple floor residential building using single line developed layout. Water from the city water mains is collected in a ground tank through a water meter and pumped to the overhead tank fitted on the top of the building. From there it is distributed to various floors as shown. Air vent pipe is provided at a height above the tank for the smooth downward flow of water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-8-rain-water-disposal-system">9.8 Rain Water Disposal System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-8-rain-water-disposal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rain water falling on roofs, paved areas and other open areas must be collected and disposed off efficiently and quickly. Plumber has to plan and fit good drainage piping system for a building. Figure 9.20 shows a sample of flat floor drainage system. The number of pipelines and the diameter has to be selected according the possible intensity of rain fall and the catchment area.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ec3c9788.jpeg" alt="img-299.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.20 Water supply system in a multifloor building.</p>
<p>The rain water falling on the roof can be collected and used after filtering. The water thus collected is good enough for drinking purpose also than the one obtained from wells and city supply lines. After the starting of a rain, allow five minutes to drain water to outside through the pipe. This cleans the surface and then the inlet valve can be opened to admit water to the tank through the filter. Figure 9.21 is self explanatory of the procedure. Collection of water by this method is called rain water harvesting for domestic use.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-5991a445.jpeg" alt="img-300.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.21 Flat roof drainage and rain harvesting system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-9-sewage-wastewater-disposal-system">9.9 Sewage/Wastewater Disposal System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-9-sewage-wastewater-disposal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The water after its use and the sewage (human excreta or soil) are collected and moved through drain pipes by gravity. Finally they are disposed to a domestic septic tank or to a public sewer. For maintaining healthy conditions in a building, a plumber has to plan and install the sewage system efficiently. Some of the important points to be considered are:</p>
<ol>
<li>The length of drainage pipe should be minimum in order to reduce the sewage handling problems. This is attained by locating the lavatory blocks at one place and one over the other for a multistoreyed building.</li>
<li>Sharp bends and more junctions should be avoided.</li>
<li>Sufficient slope for drainage has to be given for pipelines.</li>
<li>Larger diameters should be selected for pipes. Examples: 100 mm for soil pipe, 75 mm for rain water and waste water pipes, 50 mm for vent pipe, etc.</li>
<li>Enough traps should be fitted in the sewage system at suitable locations.</li>
<li>All the connections should be leak proof and manholes have to be provided at bends and intersection.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="septic-tank">Septic tank<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#septic-tank" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Solid waste carried by water in pipe lines (Sewage) is disposed in septic tanks. Figure 9.22 shows cross section and plan views of a simple septic tank with two compartments. Septic tanks are made with a minimum width of 75 cm and depth of 130 cm so that 100 cm is depth is available for water. The minimum capacity of liquid storage should be 1000 litres and the length may be 2 to 4 times the width. For circular tanks, the</p>
<p>minimum diameter shall not be less than 135 cm. The smallest size of tank is sufficient for 5 users. As the number of users increases the size of tank has to be enlarged proportionally as per the design data. The septic tanks should be plastered inside and outside with cement to make it leak proof.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-7b3954f8.jpeg" alt="img-301.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-c37f923f.jpeg" alt="img-302.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.22 Septic tank.</p>
<p>A septic tank produces septic action by anaerobic bacteria. Here carbohydrates, cellulose, proteins and fatty matter present in the sewage are broken into simple compounds and finally digested. The water separated out from the digested material is called effluent and it is disposed to below the ground level using soak pit (Seepage pit).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="soak-pit-seepage-pit">Soak pit (Seepage pit)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#soak-pit-seepage-pit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Soak pit is a covered one as shown in Figure 9.23 and the effluent is discharged to it. The earth below the tank absorbs the effluent collected in the pit. The sides of the pit may be built with bricks, stone or concrete blocks and lined with 7.5 cm coarse sand. Similar soak pits are built to dispose waste water collected form bath rooms and wash basins. They are called sludge soak pits and used separately from septic tank. Soak pits are to be located far away from the drinking water collecting well.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ce5a1a5c.jpeg" alt="img-303.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.23 Soak pit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-10-plumbing-for-industries">9.10 Plumbing for Industries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-10-plumbing-for-industries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Plumbing has many industrial applications and engineers have to design, plan, erect, test and maintain the pipe lines for various factory uses. It is crucial for moving fluids in chemical and petroleum industries in the form of raw, semi-processed and processed products. The working conditions of the pipes are also may be critical such as high pressure, vacuum, hot, cold, heavy, light, corrosive, etc. A list of the important areas of application is given below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Conveyance of oils, chemicals, water and other fluids</li>
<li>Handling of compressed air and gases</li>
<li>Steam and water handling at high pressure and temperature</li>
<li>Fluid handling in refrigeration systems</li>
<li>Waste water and chemical waste handling</li>
<li>Fire suppression systems</li>
</ol>
<p>The pipes and fittings used for the above purposes may vary according to the material moved, pressure, temperature and quantity. PVC pipes and fitting are applicable to low pressure and room temperature conditions only. As pressure and temperature increases, the pipe used may be welded G.I. or seamless stainless steel. For chemicals and large quantity supply of water or steam, cast iron pipes having in-built flanges are used. Rubber or plastic coatings of appropriate type may also be provided inside the pipes to control corrosion. Brass, lead or copper may also be selected as material, especially for high pressure low quantity movements. Industrial piping layout drawings are professionally prepared using special soft-wares designed for that. Different types of lines, symbols and colours are assigned as per International Standards to plan the layouts, so that it will be easy to read, record and understand. It is to be noted that, even though the principle of pipe installation and maintenance in industries is more or less similar to that of domestic use, the word plumbing is generally applied for buildings used for residence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-11-plumber-s-tools">9.11 Plumber's Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-11-plumber-s-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Plumbing is the process of installing, or repairing of pipes, pipe specials and fixture units for different sanitary appliances, for the supply and drain of water and gas. This includes the cutting of pipes to the required lengths, drilling of holes, threading and making of leak proof joints, etc. Sometimes bending of long pipe line may also be required. For all these</p>
<p>operations the following tools are generally used:
General fitting tools for plumbing</p>
<ol>
<li>Pliers</li>
<li>Spanners</li>
<li>Steel rule</li>
<li>Measuring tape</li>
<li>Hack saw</li>
<li>Screw drivers</li>
<li>Spirit level</li>
<li>Scriber</li>
<li>Punch</li>
<li>Electric-hand drill</li>
<li>Files</li>
</ol>
<p>Special tools for plumbing</p>
<ol>
<li>Pipe vice</li>
<li>Pipe wrench</li>
<li>Chain wrench</li>
<li>Pipe cutter</li>
<li>Pipe bending machine</li>
<li>Pipe threading dies.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pipe-vice">Pipe vice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pipe-vice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pipe vice is a device used to hold the pipe firmly while cutting, threading and fixing or loosening of pipe specials. The two jaws are V-shaped in order to grip circular pipes firmly. Figure 9.24 shows a type of pipe vice in common use.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-bfb3b2b6.jpeg" alt="img-304.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.24 Pipe vice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pipe-wrench">Pipe wrench<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pipe-wrench" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pipe wrenches are made in several designs. The most common type of pipe wrench is shown in Figure 9.25. This wrench can be used for gripping a range of pipe sizes depending upon the rack provided on the movable part of the tool. The overall length of wrench specifies the size of the tool. The commonly used size varies from 30 to 50 cm.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-c403d0e5.jpeg" alt="img-305.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.25 Pipe wrench.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chain-wrench">Chain wrench<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chain-wrench" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This wrench mainly consists of a chain for griping instead of jaws. The chain is wound around the pipe and gripped to the body of the wrench for screwing or unscrewing of large diameter pipe specials. Figure 9.26 shows the use of a chain wrench.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-c00682c9.jpeg" alt="img-306.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.26 Chain wrench.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pipe-cutter">Pipe cutter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pipe-cutter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A pipe cutter is a type of tool used by plumbers to cut pipe. Besides producing a clean cut, the tool is often a faster, cleaner, and more convenient way of cutting pipe than using a hacksaw, although this depends on the metal the pipe is made out of. There are two types of pipe cutters. Plastic tubing cutters, which really look much like a pair of pruning shears, may be used for thinner pipes and tubes such as a sprinkler pipe. Then there is a pipe cutter with a sharp wheel and adjustable jaw grips for use on thicker pipes. See Figure 9.27. These are used by rotating it around the pipe and repeatedly tightening it, until it cuts all of the way through.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-abafc71d.jpeg" alt="img-307.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.27 Pipe cutter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pipe-bending-machine">Pipe bending machine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pipe-bending-machine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bending of pipes is done by means of a pipe bending machine. It is mounted on a tripod stand and can swivel about its axis at any angle so as to give a wide range for operation. The unit can accommodate a number of bending blocks (formers) and dolly blocks to give the desired curvature at the bend. Figure 9.28 shows the top view of a hydraulic, pipe bending machine. In operation, the two outer formers remain stationary while the central former moves during the bending. To get the force for bending a hydraulic pump liver is actuated forward and backward, after closing the oil release valve.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ba130bc4.jpeg" alt="img-308.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.28 Pipe bending machine (Hydraulic).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pipe-threading-dies">Pipe threading dies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pipe-threading-dies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Dies are used to cut external threads on round pipes and rods. A die is a round block of hardened steel with hole having internal threads and flutes across the threads. The die is fitted inside a die holder called die stock and is used for cutting external threads. See Figure 9.29. In the case of cutting external threads, only one die is enough to finish the thread. To cut threads on a diameter slightly varying from the nominal diameter, an adjustable die can be used. Here, the die is split into two and a screw can be used to adjust the gap between the die pieces. The thread cutting is done after holding the pipe between the jaws of a pipe vice and screwing the die stock from the end of pipe with force.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-2dbb4ab1.jpeg" alt="img-309.jpeg">
(a) Circular split die details</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-f29a7bc5.jpeg" alt="img-310.jpeg">
(b) Circular die with holder
FIGURE 9.29 Die for threading.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-12-accessories-for-plumbing">9.12 Accessories for Plumbing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-12-accessories-for-plumbing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Plumbing process requires some accessories other than the pipes, fittings, valves and fixtures for the operation. The common accessories include:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Solvent Cement Glue: It is a PVC resin-based material used for jointing PVC pipes and pipe fittings without the use of thread. The surfaces which are in contact for a joint, are coated first with the glue. Then the parts are tightly assembled together. After drying for two minutes, the joint becomes a plastic seal and permanent leak proof one.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teflon (PTFE) Tape: It is a trade name of the DuPont company for, a non-stick substance polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE). This is available in thin tape form, which is wound over a circular ring. Joints of threaded components can be made leak proof by winding the teflon tape over the externally threaded portion, before making the joint.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shellac compound: It is a resin secreted by the female lac bug, on trees in forests. This resin is dissolved in denatured alcohol to make liquid shellac. To make leak proof joints in threaded components, a shellac mixed compound is applied on the threaded surfaces. It is allowed to dry for few minutes after making the joint. For large diameter G.I. pipes, this compound is applied on the threaded portion, after winding a thin fibre (Jute) thread for one layer. This assures a leak proof joint easily even though there is some imperfection in threading. The compound is available in small plastic bottles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gaskets: It is a mechanical seal that fills the space between two mating flat surfaces, generally to prevent leakage from or into the joined objects while under compression. Gaskets are commonly produced by cutting from sheet materials, such as gasket paper, rubber, metal, cork, felt, fibreglass, CAF (Compressed Asbestos Fibre) or a plastic polymer. In flanged pipe joints a gasket is placed in between the bolted flanges for controlling the leak. Shellac compound may also be applied on the mating surfaces.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Brushes: Small size brushes up to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>25</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">25\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">25</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  size are used for cleaning as well as application of solvent cement, shellac compound, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pipe Clips and Fixings: For fixing pipe on wall pipe clips and fixings are used. They are screwed or nailed to wall.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Backing Rings: To support heavy pipes backing rings of MS or plastic are used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wall plug or Rawl plug: It is a type of fixing used in buildings so that, screws can be fitted into masonry walls. There are many forms of wall plug, but the most common principle is to use a tapered tube of soft material, such as plastic. This is inserted loosely into a drilled hole, then a screw is tightened into the centre. The screwing action wedges the plug firmly in place and the soft material is conforming tightly to the masonry.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Screws and nails: For fixing clamps, fixtures, backing rings, etc. on wooden surfaces and walls, different types of screws and nails of various size are used in plumbing.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-13-plumbing-practice">9.13 Plumbing Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-13-plumbing-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The process of plumbing to supply water to various points in a house involves the following steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>Planning the plumbing layout: The first step of plumbing is the planning of the piping layout to fulfill the requirements in an efficient manner. For this, the distance from overhead tank to the fixtures should be the minimum as far as possible, with less head loss in pipe specials.</li>
<li>Preparation of the line sketch: After finalizing the requirements and their location, the details are worked out and isometric single line layout is prepared. This should include the dimensions and size of pipes, pipe specials, fixtures etc.</li>
<li>List of materials and their collection: A detailed list of materials with specification is prepared and those items are collected in the site.</li>
<li>Installation: The fixtures are installed in the specified positions and the pipe line paths are marked. Starting from the tank, the pipes are laid by joining the pipe specials one by one. For this the pipes are to be cut to required lengths considering the overlaps. Hacksaw or pipe cutter may be used for this. PVC pipes and specials are joined by solvent cement application. For GI pipes, threading is to be done using dies and they are joined by screwing together with the use of pipe specials. The installation is completed using various tools and accessories.</li>
<li>Inspection and testing: The last step of plumbing is inspection of the installation and testing. After checking each joint and clamping the pipes in position, water line is opened from the tank to section by section, in order to test the working of fixtures and pipe lines. If there is any leak or fault is found, that should be rectified after closing the supply valve.</li>
</ol>
<p>Plumbing processes and the steps are almost similar for other requirements like rain water disposal and sewage disposal. Here, the pipe diameters are large as 50 mm to 150 mm depending on the use. Proper slope and air vents have to be provided to pipe lines to result defect free working of the system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cutting-to-lengths-and-end-threading-of-gi-pipes">Cutting to lengths and end-threading of GI pipes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cutting-to-lengths-and-end-threading-of-gi-pipes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>GI pipes are galvanized mild steel (coated with zinc) pipes and used for conveying raw and treated drinking water. Mostly medium quality GI pipes are used. Their sizes vary from 15 mm to 150 mm. These pipes are manufactured conforming to IS-1239 (pt-I) 1990. Table 9.1 gives the nominal bore size and the corresponding useful data used for plumbing.</p>
<p>Table 9.1 Dimensions, nominal mass and thread size of medium quality steel pipes</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Nominal bore</th><th></th><th>Outside</th><th></th><th>Thickness</th><th></th><th>Weight</th><th></th><th>Thread</th><th></th><th>Major</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>mm</td><td>inch</td><td></td><td>Dia. mm</td><td></td><td>(Std.) mm</td><td></td><td>kg/m</td><td></td><td>per inch</td><td></td><td>Dia. mm</td></tr><tr><td>15</td><td>1/2</td><td></td><td>21.3</td><td></td><td>2.77</td><td></td><td>1.27</td><td></td><td>14</td><td></td><td>20.955</td></tr><tr><td>20</td><td>3/4</td><td></td><td>26.7</td><td></td><td>2.87</td><td></td><td>1.69</td><td></td><td>14</td><td></td><td>26.441</td></tr><tr><td>25</td><td>1</td><td></td><td>33.4</td><td></td><td>3.38</td><td></td><td>2.50</td><td></td><td>11</td><td></td><td>33.249</td></tr><tr><td>40</td><td>1^{1}/_{2}</td><td></td><td>48.3</td><td></td><td>3.68</td><td></td><td>4.05</td><td></td><td>11</td><td></td><td>47.803</td></tr><tr><td>50</td><td>2</td><td></td><td>60.3</td><td></td><td>3.91</td><td></td><td>5.44</td><td></td><td>11</td><td></td><td>59.614</td></tr><tr><td>65</td><td>2^{1}/_{2}</td><td></td><td>75.9</td><td></td><td>5.16</td><td></td><td>8.62</td><td></td><td>11</td><td></td><td>75.184</td></tr><tr><td>80</td><td>3</td><td></td><td>88.9</td><td></td><td>5.49</td><td></td><td>11.29</td><td></td><td>11</td><td></td><td>87.884</td></tr><tr><td>100</td><td>4</td><td></td><td>114.3</td><td></td><td>6.02</td><td></td><td>16.07</td><td></td><td>11</td><td></td><td>113.03</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>To cut a full length pipe to required length, it is gripped horizontally between the jaws of a pipe vise and cut to length using a hack saw or a pipe cutter. The bur formed at the cut end should be removed using a file. For cutting thread on the pipe, the die size of major diameter</p>
<p>(suitable to the outside diameter) is selected first as given in Table 9.1. Then the split die diameter is slightly enlarged by adjusting the grub screws on it (Figure 9.29) to accommodate the outside diameter of pipe. The die is screwed forward gradually from the end of pipe so that, a rough thread with less depth is formed first. While cutting, the screwing action may be forward and backward to remove the chip easily. The grub screws of the dies are tightened step by step to get full depth of thread. To check the fitness of thread, a standard coupler of same size may be screwed on the pipe using a wrench. Internal threads are not cut usually on pipes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example-1">Example 1<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Prepare a double line piping layout for the given sketch (Figure 9.30) and make the pipe line assembly using PVC pipe fittings as per the given dimensions and size.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-of-operations">List of operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-of-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Copy the given single line sketch in the work record.</li>
<li>Convert the sketch to double line piping layout as shown in Figure 9.31.</li>
<li>Mark the lengths on pipe after adding the overlaps for specials and cut it into pieces precisely using hack saw. The cut ends should be perpendicular to the axis of pipe and bur free. File may be used for correcting that.</li>
<li>Assemble the fittings, check the accuracy and apply corrections if required.</li>
<li>Apply solvent cement on the mating surfaces using brush and assemble the components together to complete the required pipe line work.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-b8ddac0a.jpeg" alt="img-312.jpeg">

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Prepare a line sketch of the layout in the work record and mark the important parts on them as shown in Figure 9.32.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-929ae3e9.jpeg" alt="img-313.jpeg">
FIGURE 9.32 Assembly of WC and flush tank.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Fix the European water closet on the floor, leaving sufficient space to accommodate the flush tank on the wall. Two holes have to be drilled on the floor for this purpose and screws have to be tightened to the plugs inserted in the holes.</li>
<li>Mark the position of the L-clamps on the wall relative to the WC and drill four holes using hand drill. Insert the PVC plugs in the holes and tighten screws to fix the clamps in position. Place the flush tank on the clamp and check the location.</li>
<li>Locate the position of angle valve relative to the flush tank and fix the in coming pipe and the valve on it.</li>
<li>Connect the incoming and outgoing flexible pipes to the flush tank using tools.</li>
<li>The joints are made leak proof by applying solvent cement on mating surfaces of PVC fittings. The connection between WC and waste pipe is sealed using white cement in paste form.</li>
<li>Assemble the seat and seat cover over the WC using the fixing screws.</li>
<li>After checking the assembly of the WC and the flush tank, including the float setting for its closing at filled position, water line is connected to the angle valve.</li>
<li>The assembly is tested for its working.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example-3">Example 3<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-3" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cut the given GI pipe of diameter 3/4" (20 mm) to 150 mm length and cut standard pipe thread on the cut end. Also check the accuracy of the thread by screwing a GI elbow of the same size on the end.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim">Aim<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To cut the given GI pipe of diameter 3/4" (20 mm) to 150 mm length and cut standard pipe thread on the cut end. Also check the accuracy of the thread by screwing an elbow of the same size on the end.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="materials-required">Materials required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#materials-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tools-required">Tools required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>

<li>Hack saw</li>
<li>File</li>
<li>Pipe wrench</li>
<li>Steel rule</li>
<li>Scriber</li>
<li>Threading die 3/4" (20 mm) with holder.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-of-operations">List of operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-of-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Sketching of the joint</li>
<li>Marking of length</li>
<li>Cutting of GI pipe into length</li>
<li>End finishing</li>
<li>Screwing of elbow</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Sketch the pipe assembly view in the work record as shown in the Figure 9.33.</li>
<li>Mark the length 150 mm on the GI pipe using steel rule and scriber.</li>
<li>Hold the pipe on the vice and cut the pipe to the required length using hack saw.</li>
<li>File the end of pipe to remove bur as well as to form a slight</li>
</ol>
<p>taper around to admit the die.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Select the die for 3/4" (20 mm) thread and fit inside the die holder. Unscrew the grub screws slightly to enlarge the die hole in order to accommodate outer diameter of the pipe.</li>
<li>Start cutting of thread gradually from the slightly tapered end of pipe by screwing forward and then backward.</li>
<li>Do the same operation for the required full length. Then tighten the grub screws and cut the thread two three times to get the full depth for thread.</li>
<li>Screw the elbow to the full length using pipe wrench and get the work finished.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-9350c4fd.jpeg" alt="img-314.jpeg">
(a) Pipe end</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-75eccfdc.jpeg" alt="img-315.jpeg">
(b) Pipe assembly
FIGURE 9.33 GI pipe with elbow.</p>
