<p>Module</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="machining-processes">Machining Processes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#machining-processes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>10</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="turning">Turning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#turning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Turning is a metal-cutting process in which the workpiece is rotated and a single-point cutting tool of hard material is brought to the surface by feed motion resulting the removal of excess metal in the form of chips. Lathe is the name of the machine used for turning process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="10-1-introduction-to-turning">10.1 Introduction to Turning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-1-introduction-to-turning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="10-1-1-principle-of-turning">10.1.1 Principle of Turning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-1-1-principle-of-turning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Turning is one of the oldest machining operations and the machine used for turning is called lathe. The present form of lathe was developed initially by Henry Maudsley in 1800, for cutting threads. The principle of turning is explained Figure 10.1. The workpiece is gripped by a rotating fixture called chuck fitted on the spindle of the lathe headstock. The other end of the workpiece is supported by the centre fitted on the tailstock of the lathe. A cutting tool is fixed on a tool post, which can move parallel to the axis of rotation for feed motion. By this machining, a cylindrical external surface is formed. Turning is basically the machining of external cylindrical forms. The same process in lathe can be modified by changing the tool position, by changing the type of tool and the tool movements to produce various shapes like step, taper, flat surface, spherical surface, screw thread, groove, hole, undercut, etc.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-98667c24.jpeg" alt="img-318.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.1 Principle of turning (Top view).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="10-1-2-metal-cutting-and-chip-formation">10.1.2 Metal Cutting and Chip Formation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-1-2-metal-cutting-and-chip-formation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Metal-cutting operation in turning is explained by Figure 10.2. The workpiece rotates about the centre of it and the sharp tip of the cutting tool is pressed on the cutting surface along the horizontal centre line. This makes a layer of metal to separate from the surface in the form of chips and moves along the rake surface of the tool. The angle made by the top surface of the tool (rake surface) to the horizontal centre line of the work is known as the rake angle of cutting. Many cutting properties, including the cutting force, are governed by this rake angle of tool. In order to avoid rubbing of the machined surface on the cutting tool, a small relief angle is given to the end for clearance.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-7024ba9a.jpeg" alt="img-319.jpeg"></p>
<p>The type of chip produced during turning depends on the material being cut and the cutting conditions. The conditions include the feed rate, depth of cut, the type of tool, the type of machine tool and the presence of cutting lubricant. The types of chip formed during turning (Figure 10.3) are:</p>
<p>(a) Continuous chip
(b) Discontinuous chip
(c) Continuous chip with built-up edge</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-f54ec3c4.jpeg" alt="img-320.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.2 Metal cutting in lathe.
FIGURE 10.3 Types of chips.</p>
<p>A continuous chip is formed by plastic deformation of metal, without fracture, in front of the cutting edge of the tool. It is followed by a smooth flow of the chip along the tool rake face. While machining the ductile materials like mild steel, copper, and aluminium at correct cutting speed and feed, a ribbon like continuous chip is obtained. While cutting brittle materials like cast iron and cast brass, segmental chips are formed. The built up edge associated with a continuous chip is a result of welding particles of workpiece as hard edge at high pressure and temperature. The formation of built up edge reduces the sharpness of tool resulting high cutting force and temperature. The surface finish of machined surface is also reduced. The formation of built up edge can be minimized or prevented by giving light cuts at high speeds in the presence of a good lubricant.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="10-1-3-cutting-speeds-for-turning">10.1.3 Cutting Speeds for Turning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-1-3-cutting-speeds-for-turning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The cutting speed (cutting velocity) for machining is represented as the surface velocity of the workpiece in motion.</p>
<p>Cutting velocity,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi><mo>=</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi><mo>×</mo><mi>D</mi><mo>×</mo><mi>N</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>1000</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{V} = \mathrm{r} \times D \times N / 1000 \mathrm{~m} / \mathrm{min}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">V</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord mathrm">r</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span><span class="mord">/1000</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">m</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">min</span></span></span></span></span></span> .</p>
<p>where</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">D</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span></span></span></span></span>  is the diameter of work in mm</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>N</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">N</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">N</span></span></span></span></span>  is the rpm of work.</p>
<p>The cutting velocity of workpiece is selected by the following factors.</p>
<ol>
<li>The physical property of the work material like hardness brittleness, ductility, etc.</li>
<li>The material property of cutting tool.</li>
<li>The feed and depth of cut.</li>
<li>The rigidity and capacity of the machine tool to resist the cutting forces.</li>
</ol>
<p>A calculation method of finding the approximate cutting speed, feed and depth of turning is given as:</p>
<p>cutting speed,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>C</mi><mo>×</mo><msup><mi>A</mi><mrow><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>3</mn></mrow></msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V = C\times A^{1 / 3}\mathrm{m / min}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.138em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.888em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1/3</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">m/min</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>where,</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span>  Constant depends on the material cut</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span>  Area of cut</p>
<p>= (Feed per rev.)  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>×</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\times</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6667em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">×</span></span></span></span></span>  depth of cut mm².</p>
<p>The table below gives the value of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span></span></span></span></span> , and  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span></span></span></span></span>  for the materials generally turned in lathe using tool of material of High Speed Steel.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Work material</th><th>V (m/min)</th><th>C (constant)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Mild steel</td><td>20 to 28</td><td>24</td></tr><tr><td>High carbon steel</td><td>12 to 18</td><td>13</td></tr><tr><td>Cast iron</td><td>18 to 25</td><td>18</td></tr><tr><td>Brass</td><td>45 to 90</td><td>48</td></tr><tr><td>Bronze</td><td>15 to 21</td><td>21</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The depth of cut for rough turning can be taken as 0.8 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>6</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">6\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  in medium size machine tools and feed per revolution is taken between 0.1 to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span> .</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="10-1-4-types-of-turning-machines">10.1.4 Types of Turning Machines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-1-4-types-of-turning-machines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Lathe is the family name for the machine tools used for turning operations. There are many types of lathes by design, size, use automation, etc. A list of the names of lathes used in workshops and production centres is given below:</p>
<p>(a) General purpose lathes</p>
<ol>
<li>Centre (Engine) lathe</li>
<li>Speed lathe</li>
<li>Bench lathe</li>
<li>Tool room lathe</li>
</ol>
<p>(b) Special purpose lathes</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Facing lathe</li>
<li>Boring lathe</li>
<li>Turret lathe</li>
<li>Capstan lathe</li>
</ol>
<p>(c) Mass-production lathes</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>Automatic screw cutting lathe</li>
<li>Swiss-type automatic lathe</li>
<li>Single-spindle automatic lathe</li>
<li>Multi-spindle automatic lathe</li>
</ol>
<p>Centre lathe or engine lathe is the most common machine tool used for various turning operations. It is popular in work shops for producing or repairing cylindrical parts in small quantities. A student in engineering has to study in detail about and practice in a centre lathe. Speed lathes are similar to the centre lathes working at high speeds. They are generally used for wood turning. Bench lathe is a small size lathe fitted on a work table and used to produce very small size components. Tool room lathes are used in tool rooms for repairing or producing accurate size of tools and small size of components.</p>
<p>Lathes of special category are designed for a particular range of turning operations only. A facing lathe, for example, is used for cutting large size gears, discs, etc. which require mainly the facing operation. Boring lathes are suitable for shaping the large size holes. Turret and capstan lathes are designed for batch production of small and medium size components in a semiautomatic manner. For mass production of cylindrical parts, the production lathes are employed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="10-2-centre-lathe-engine-lathe">10.2 Centre Lathe (Engine Lathe)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-2-centre-lathe-engine-lathe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Centre lathe is a machine tool used for turning (machining) to produce various cylindrical shapes. The workpiece is placed between two centres of the machine, one is the driving centre, which is the nose of a rotating spindle supported inside the headstock. The other one is a dead centre called tailstock. In olden times, steam engine was used as the prime mover for running the machine tool and hence this lathe was called as engine lathe. Pedal operated small size lathes were also used in those days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-layout-and-specification">General layout and specification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-layout-and-specification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The general layout of a centre lathe is shown in Figure 10.4. This machine tool mainly consists of a horizontal bed which forms the body of the machine. The driving centre called head-stock is mounted on the left end. The head-stock has a horizontal spindle rotated by a prime mover (motor) and it carries a face plate or chuck to hold the workpiece. On the right side there is the tailstock having dead centre to support the end of rotating workpiece. The cutting tool is fixed on a tool post which is mounted above a sliding member called carriage. With the help of the carriage, the tool is moved longitudinally parallel to the axis of rotation and in the cross direction of it, to get the cutting action.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-9fd58f64.jpeg" alt="img-321.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.4 General layout of a centre lathe.</p>
<p>The size of a centre lathe is specified by giving the following details:</p>
<ol>
<li>The maximum centre to centre distance in mm, i.e., the maximum length of workpiece that can be accommodated between the centres.</li>
<li>The swing or maximum diameter that can be rotated over the bed ways.</li>
<li>The length of the bed including the head stock and tail stock lengths.</li>
<li>The diameter of the hole through the lathe spindle for turning round bars.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bed">Bed<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The bed of a lathe is the body of the lathe made up of cast iron. All other parts are fitted on the bed. There are the guideways on the top side of the bed on which the carriage or saddle moves parallel to the axis of rotation of the spindle of lathe. The tailstock is fitted on the right side of it and the headstock on its left end. A detailed layout of a lathe is given in Figure 10.5.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-468cdb6f.jpeg" alt="img-322.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.5 Centre lathe (Name of parts).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="headstock">Headstock<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#headstock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Headstock of a lathe is the power source for the machine tool. The prime mover (motor) is usually fitted at the bottom side and is connected to the spindle of lathe using flat or V-belt on stepped pulleys. In modern lathes, gears are also used to get large speed ranges. The spindle carrying the work revolves inside heavy duty bearings in the headstock.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tailstock">Tailstock<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tailstock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The right end (outer end) of the work is supported by a stationary (dead) centre called tailstock. The main function of a tailstock is to hold the dead centre which supports one end of the work. Its position can be adjusted and clamped on the bed. Figure 10.6 shows cross section of a tailstock.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-8d37d798.jpeg" alt="img-323.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.6 Tailstock (Sectional view).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="carriage">Carriage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carriage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The carriage placed on the bed in between the headstock and tailstock supports, guides and controls the movements of the cutting tool. It consists of several sets of parts like apron, saddle, cross slide, compound rest and tool post.</p>
<ol>
<li>Apron: It is the lower vertical portion of the carriage hanging on the saddle and contains the controls for the tool movements and carriage movements. Apron contains gears and clutches for transmitting motion from the feed rod to the carriage. The split nut mechanism which</li>
</ol>
<p>engages with the lead screw, gives the movements of tool for thread-cutting.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Saddle: This is an 'H' shaped cast frame which is resting flat over the bed. This part slides directly over the guideways. The apron is hanging from the front edge of it. The cross slide, the compound rest and the tool post are fitted over this. Figure 10.7 gives the layout of the arrangement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cross slide: The cross slide mounted over the saddle enables the cross movement to the tool post. In order to move the cross slide forward or backward, the screw fitted below it, is turned by rotating the handle provided at the end of it. When the screw rotates, it moves through a nut which is fitted below the cross slide, resulting the cross movement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Compound rest: The compound rest or compound slide is fitted over the cross slide. This has a circular base to obtain angular movements. The compound slide has a screw and nut arrangement to get forward and backward movements for short lengths.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-39ec0a23.jpeg" alt="img-324.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.7 Carriage assembly.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Tool post: The tool post is mounted on the top of the compound rest. The tool is fixed on the tool post for cutting action. There are different types of tool posts in use. They may be grouped as mentioned below:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Single screw tool post</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Four screw tool post</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open side tool post</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Four way tool post</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Figure 10.8 shows a single screw tool post used in small and medium-size centre lathes. This mainly consists of a tool post body of round bar with slotted hole for fixing the tool. The tool is fixed over a convex rocker which is placed over a concave ring washer, using a tool post screw. The convex rocker and the concave ring enable to fix the cutting point of tool at the horizontal centre line of the workpiece and to adjust the effective rake angle of tool.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-a4a297eb.jpeg" alt="img-325.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.8 Single screw tool post.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="end-of-bed-gearing">End of bed gearing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#end-of-bed-gearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The spindle motion is transferred to the feed gear box through gears fitted at the left end of the lathe bed. The drive is then transmitted through the feed gear box, selectively to the lead screw or the feed shaft, depending on whether the machine is being used for thread-cutting or plain-turning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="10-3-accessories-and-attachments">10.3 Accessories and Attachments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-3-accessories-and-attachments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To use lathe for various turning operations, the accessories are also required in addition to the main parts explained so far. The commonly used accessories are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Face plate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Four-jaw chuck</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Three-jaw chuck</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Centres</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Carriers and catch plates</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Steady rest</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Follow rest</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Service tools</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The accessories include the following items also, which support the turning operation directly or indirectly:</p>
<ol>
<li>Machine lamp</li>
<li>Splash guard</li>
<li>Coolant equipment</li>
<li>Mandrels</li>
<li>Magnetic chuck</li>
<li>Collet chuck</li>
<li>Drill holder</li>
<li>Change gears</li>
</ol>
<p>The attachments used in a lathe are additional equipment required for special operations. They include the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Taper turning attachment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hydro-copying attachment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Milling attachment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Face plate: A face plate basically consists of a circular disc with a central-threaded hole to fit on the spindle nose. There are radial slots and T-slots to fix the clamps (Figure 10.9). Face plate is used to hold workpiece which cannot be held by centres or chucks.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-8969e9db.jpeg" alt="img-326.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.9 Face plate.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Four-jaw chuck: A chuck is a work-holding device used in lathes. The four-jaw chuck shown in Figure 10.10 has four independent jaws which are usually used to grip the workpiece of shapes other than cylindrical. The body of the chuck is made of cast iron, while the jaws are made of hard steel.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-5fbadcd8.jpeg" alt="img-327.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.10 Four-jaw chuck.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Three-jaw chuck: Figure 10.11 shows a self-centring three-jaw chuck. The jaws are moved simultaneously by screwing one jaw. This enables easy clamping of cylindrical jobs at its centre. The scroll disc having spiral grooves enables the simultaneous movement of the jaws.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-e7380b8d.jpeg" alt="img-328.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.11 Three-jaw chuck.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Centres: The centre used to support long rods may be of live centre or dead centre. The centres are made of hard material and are machined to smooth surface. The included angle of the centre is usually kept as <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>60</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">60^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. Figure 10.12 shows different types of centres used in a lathe.</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Ordinary centre</p>
<p>(b) Ball centre</p>
<p>(c) Friction less centre</p>
<p>(d) Half centre</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Carrier and catch plate: Carrier and catch plate arrangement is used while machining jobs between centres. Carrier or driving dog is attached to the end of the workpiece by set screws and catch plate is either screwed or bolted to the nose of the spindle of headstock (Figure 10.13).</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-93f651bc.jpeg" alt="img-329.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.12 Centres.
(a) Catch plate (single pin type)
FIGURE 10.13 Catch plate and carrier.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-06c66305.jpeg" alt="img-330.jpeg">
(b) Straight tail carrier (driving dog)</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Steady rest: A rest is a device used to support cylindrical, lengthy, and slender jobs (Figure 10.14). A steady rest is a mechanical frame of the type shown in figure which acts as an intermediate bearing having three-point support to resist the cutting forces. It is mounted on the bed guideways.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-15ad5d60.jpeg" alt="img-331.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.14 Steady rest.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Fallow rest: This rest is similar to that of steady rest. The unit is clamped on the carriage so that it follows when the carriage moves during cutting operation. This unit has only two points to support the work.</li>
<li>Service tools: The service tools used in lathe include spanners, screw drivers, pliers, allen keys, etc. They are explained with figures in Chapter 3 for fitting.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="10-4-tools-for-measuring-and-machining">10.4 Tools for Measuring and Machining<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-4-tools-for-measuring-and-machining" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="10-4-1-measuring-and-marking-tools">10.4.1 Measuring and Marking Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-4-1-measuring-and-marking-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The tools used for measuring and marking dimensions on the workpiece during turning are almost the same as that are used for fitting. A list of the frequently used measuring and marking tool are given below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Steel rule</li>
<li>Vernier calliper</li>
<li>Micro meter</li>
<li>Outside and inside callipers</li>
<li>Divider</li>
<li>Combination set</li>
<li>Vernier height gauge</li>
<li>Screw gauge</li>
<li>Punches</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="10-scribers">10. Scribers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-scribers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>For explanation and figures, refer Chapter 3 for fitting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="10-4-2-cutting-tools">10.4.2 Cutting Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-4-2-cutting-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tool-geometry">Tool geometry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tool-geometry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Single-point cutting tools are used for turning operations. There are a number of forms of single-point cutting tools in use. The tool geometry of a standard single-point right hand cutting tool is given in Figure 10.15. It has a shank of rectangular cross section. The cutting point has a radius called nose radius. The top face on which the chip is rubbing is called rake face. The angle of it with respect to the horizontal centre line of the job is called the effective rake angle. The rake angle value has much importance on the cutting forces. The metal is actually removed by the side cutting edge and the nose. The relief angles give clearances, so that rubbing of tool on the cut surface is avoided. The approximate values of the angles and nose radius of a single point HSS tool for cutting mild steel are as follows:</p>
<p>Front as well as side rake angles  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>10</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">= 10</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span></span></span></span></span>  to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>12</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">12^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>Front as well as side clearance angles  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>6</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">= 6</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span></span></span></span></span>  to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>8</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">8^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">8</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>The nose radius  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0.4</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">= 0.4\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0.4</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span>  to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1.6</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.6\mathrm{mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1.6</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-9cdac7b2.jpeg" alt="img-332.jpeg">
FIGURE 10.15 Single point cutting tool (right hand type).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-cutting-tools">Types of cutting tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-cutting-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>For producing different shapes in turning, tools in various forms are required. The common forms of cutting tools in use are given below (Figure 10.16).</p>
<ol>
<li>Cylindrical turning tool: It is used for rough and finish turning of cylindrical surfaces.</li>
<li>Facing tool: This tool is used to produce flat face perpendicular to the axis of rotation.</li>
<li>Grooving tool: It is used to produce grooves of different shapes.</li>
<li>Parting off tool: It is used to part off the job from the stock by narrow groove cutting.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-81b69f9c.jpeg" alt="img-333.jpeg">
(a) Parting off tool</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-291d2030.jpeg" alt="img-334.jpeg">
(b) Thread cutting tool</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-ad90505c.jpeg" alt="img-335.jpeg">
(c) Boring tool
FIGURE 10.16 Types of turning tools.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-a1d30d99.jpeg" alt="img-336.jpeg">
(d) Turning tool (right hand type)
(e) Turning tool (left hand type)</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Chamfering tool: It is used to produce chamfer at the required angle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shoulder turning tool: It is used to produce sharp curved or grooved shoulders.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Forming tool: It is used to produce curved profiles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>External thread cutting tool: It is used to turn V-shaped external threads.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Square thread cutting tool: It is used to turn square threads.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Internal thread cutting tool: It is used to cut internal threads on jobs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drilling tool: It is used to twist drill with taper shank to produce holes by fixing it on the tail stock.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Boring tool: It is used to enlarge the hole size by internal turning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Under cutting tool: It is used to produce undercuts in side holes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right hand tool: Any tool shape which is used to cut from tailstock (right side) to the headstock side is right hand tool.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Left hand tool: Any tool shape which is used to cut from headstock (left side) to the tailstock side is left hand tool.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Knurling tool: This tool is used to get knurled surface used for handle grip.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thread chaser: This is a multipoint threading tool used to correct the thread shape.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Combination centre drill: It is used to make a 60° conical hole at the centre of a shaft for supporting at dead centre of the tailstock.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Files: It is used to make smooth external surfaces by filing during turning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Emery paper: It is used to make very smooth surfaces by manual application during turning.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The cutting tools are made by any one of the following methods.</p>
<ol>
<li>Forged tool: The shape is made by forging, heat treatment and griding.</li>
<li>Tipped tools by brazing: Tool tips of higher hardness are brazed to the shank for holding.</li>
<li>Tipped tool by screwing: The tool tips are fixed to the holder by screwed fasteners.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tool-material">Tool material<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tool-material" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Turning tools are made by using various hard materials of the following types.</p>
<ol>
<li>High carbon steels</li>
<li>High speed steels (HSS)</li>
<li>Cast nonferrous alloys</li>
<li>Carbides</li>
<li>Ceramic tools</li>
<li>Diamond.</li>
</ol>
<p>More about these material are given in Chapter 1 under the title cutting tool materials.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="10-5-turning-operations">10.5 Turning Operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-5-turning-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The turning operations which are commonly conducted in a workshop can be grouped according to the work holding method as mentioned below:</p>
<ol>
<li>These are held between the centres and driven by carrier and catch plate.</li>
<li>These are held and driven by chuck on one end and the other end supported by tailstock dead centre.</li>
<li>These are held and driven by chuck or face plate alone.</li>
<li>These are held on a mandrel which is supported by centres and driven by carrier and catch plate.</li>
</ol>
<p>The turning operations which are performed in a lathe depending on the method of removal of metal can be listed as shown below:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-general">A. General<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-general" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>External turning</li>
<li>Shoulder turning</li>
<li>Facing</li>
<li>Chamfering</li>
<li>Grooving</li>
<li>Forming</li>
<li>Taper turning</li>
<li>Parting off</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-general-internal-turning">B. General internal turning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-general-internal-turning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Boring</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Counter boring</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Undercutting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taper boring.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-special-turning-operations">C. Special turning operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-special-turning-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>External thread cutting</li>
<li>Internal thread cutting</li>
<li>Drilling</li>
<li>Reaming</li>
<li>Knurling</li>
<li>Tapping</li>
<li>Eccentric turning</li>

</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="10-6-turning-practice">10.6 Turning Practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#10-6-turning-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="example">Example<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="aim">Aim<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="material-required">Material required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#material-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Workpiece material: Mild steel round rod</p>
<p>Workpiece size: 30 mm diameter and 150 mm length</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="tools-required">Tools required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tools-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ol>
<li>Centre lathe fitted with 3 jaw chuck,</li>
<li>Cutting tool,</li>
<li>Centre drill,</li>
<li>Spanner,</li>
<li>Steel rule,</li>
<li>Vernier calliper,</li>
<li>Outside calliper,</li>
<li>Micrometer.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="list-operations">List operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ol>
<li>Facing the stock end,</li>
<li>Centre drilling,</li>
<li>Rough turning of cylindrical surfaces and steps,</li>
<li>Finish turning of cylindrical surfaces and steps.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ol>
<li>Copy the given drawing in the work record.</li>
<li>Collect the tools and the blank piece.</li>
<li>Check the size of the blank using steel rule and outside calliper for its suitability to make the model as per drawing.</li>
<li>Grip the blank piece in the three-jaw chuck projecting a short length of about 20 mm from the jaws.</li>
<li>Fix the cutting tool on the tool post keeping the cutting point at the height of the axis of rotation. This can be done by setting the tool at the height of nose point of the dead centre.</li>
<li>Turn the end face by facing operation and drill at the centre using centre drill, after fixing the drill bit on the tailstock.</li>
<li>Re-clamp the workpiece on the chuck such that the blank is projecting approximately 120 mm from the jaws and the other end is supported by the dead centre of the tailstock.</li>
<li>Do the rough straight turning of diameter 25 mm at a low rpm (300 rpm to get a cutting velocity of about 25 m/min).</li>
<li>Do the rough turning of diameter 15 mm at about 400 rpm.</li>
<li>Finish the cylindrical surface and the step face at high rpm (600 rpm to get a cutting velocity of about 50 m/min). Check the dimensions and unclamp the workpiece from the lathe.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-1-process-chart">A.1 Process Chart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-1-process-chart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A process chart is a document in tabular form which furnishes all the operations to be performed on a workpiece. The other names called for the tabular form are operation process chart, operation sheet, worksheet, etc. Process charts are commonly used in production shops to give instructions to machine operators.</p>
<p>Table A.1 shows a process chart suitable to prepare a turning model in machine shop. A process chart should contain all the information about the workpiece, like material, blank size, weight, etc. and the details about the machines used, departments, and so on. A drawing of the component with full dimensions, tolerances and surface finish should be attached. The production operations are carried out in sequence as shown in the process chart shown in Figure A.1 and they are numbered as 05, 10, 15, 20, etc. The cycle time and total number of operations should be determined from the details. A student has to copy the drawing of model and prepare the chart in the workbook before starting operations on the machine tool.</p>
<p>Table A.1 Process Chart</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Name of part: Model No:</th><th></th><th>M/c No: Department:</th><th></th><th>Material: Blank size:</th><th></th><th>Total operations: Cycle time:</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Operation seq.</td><td>Operation details (Clamping, feed, depth of cut, etc.)</td><td>Tools/Gauges</td><td>Cutting</td><td></td><td>Set up time (min)</td><td>Operational time (min)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td>Speed m/min</td><td></td><td></td><td>r.p.m.</td></tr><tr><td>05</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>15</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>20</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Name of student: Class and Registration No:</td><td></td><td></td><td>Approved by: (Signature) Name of staff:</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-2-quality-assessment-chart">A.2 Quality Assessment Chart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-2-quality-assessment-chart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The dimensions on a workpiece can be named as D1, D2, D3, ... for diameters and L1, L2, L3, ... for lengths. As per the tolerance given (general tolerance or tolerance shown using ISO symbols) the upper and lower limits of each dimension can be calculated and tabulated as displayed in Table A.2. The actual values measured by the student on his model can also be entered, so that the teacher can evaluate the quality of performance.</p>
<p>Table A.2 Quality assessment chart</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="second-edition">SECOND EDITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-edition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanical-workshop-practice">MECHANICAL WORKSHOP PRACTICE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanical-workshop-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="k-c-john">K.C. JOHN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#k-c-john" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Designed for the core course on Workshop Practice offered to all first-year diploma and degree level students of engineering, this book presents clear and concise explanation of the basic principles of manufacturing processes and equips students with overall knowledge of engineering materials, tools and equipment commonly used in the engineering field.</p>
<p>The book describes the general principles of different workshop processes such as primary and secondary shaping processes, metal joining methods, surface finishing and heat treatment. The workshop processes covered also include the hand-working processes such as benchwork, fitting, arc welding, sheet metal work, carpentry, blacksmithy and foundry. It also explains the importance of safety measures to be followed in workshop processes and details the procedure of writing the records of the practices. The tools and equipment used in each hand-working process are enumerated before elaborating the process. Finally, the book discusses the machining processes such as turning operations, the cutting tools and the tools used for measuring and marking, and explains the working principle of Engine Lathe. An appendix for advanced level practice and assessment of work has also been included.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="new-to-this-edition">NEW TO THIS EDITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#new-to-this-edition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A separate chapter on Plumbing as per the revised syllabus of Indian Universities</li>
<li>Method for sketching isometric single line piping layout</li>
<li>Neatly-drawn illustrations and examples on Plumbing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="key-features">KEY FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Follows the International Standard Organization (ISO) code of practice for drawings.</li>
<li>Includes a large number of illustrations to explain the methods and processes discussed.</li>
<li>Contains chapter-end questions for viva voce test and exercises for making models.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-author">THE AUTHOR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-author" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>K.C. John is Professor and Head, Department of Mechanical Engineering, Jyothi Engineering College, Cheruthuruthy, Thrissur, Kerala. He has also served Vidya Academy of Science and Technology, Thalakkottukara, Thrissur, Kerala. He has more than 35 years of teaching experience including overseas assignments. Professor John is a Fellow member of the Institution of Engineers (India) and Indian Society for Technical Education (ISTE). He is the author of several books. His books titled Textbook of Machine Drawing, Engineering Graphics for Degree, and Engineering Graphics for Diploma have been published by PHI Learning, New Delhi.</p>
